### [1] [Decay and structure of heavy flavour](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18098)
*Stefan Groote,Arpan Chatterjee,Maria Naeem*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This talk provides an overview of Tartu working group's research within the COST action CA24159, covering charmed baryon production/decays via current algebra and tensor invariants, CP violation through long-distance rescattering, neutron beta decay and polarized W boson decays using helicity formalism, identical-particle/mass effects in Higgs→4ℓ, intrinsic charm discrepancies (SELEX vs. LHCb), and a nonlocal NJL+Faddeev framework for hadron structure.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To introduce Tartu working group's contributions to the COST action CA24159 on hadron structure and spectroscopy, addressing open problems including CP violation in charmed baryons, anomalies in intrinsic charm measurements, and theoretical descriptions of hadrons beyond local effective models.

Method: Current algebra with tensor invariants for nonleptonic decays; helicity formalism for neutron beta decay and polarized W decay; analysis of identical-particle statistics and mass effects in Higgs→4ℓ; nonlocal field operators and nonlocal Nambu–Jona-Lasinio model derived from QCD, combined with relativistic Faddeev equations for hadronic bound states.

Result: A unified framework linking long-distance CP violation in charmed baryons to rescattering; demonstration that helicity methods apply broadly (e.g., radiative corrections to W decay); identification of identical-particle and mass effects as relevant in Higgs→4ℓ; resolution of SELEX–LHCb intrinsic charm discrepancy via nonlocality; successful description of hadronic states using nonlocal NJL + Faddeev approach.

Conclusion: Nonlocality and advanced symmetry-based methods (current algebra, helicity, Faddeev) are essential for consistent treatment of hadron production, decay, spectroscopy, and CP violation; several open questions remain regarding intrinsic charm, hadron structure, and precision SM tests within the COST action.

Abstract: In accordance to the aim of the constituing meeting of the COST action CA24159 ``Structure and Spectroscopy of Hadrons Research Project'' to introduce the different groups to the action, in this talk we give an overview over the subjects dealt with by the working group in Tartu related to hadron physics. We deal with the production and the nonleptonic decays of charmed baryons in the framework of the current algebra approach in terms of tensor invariants and explain how this approach can be used to approach CP violation via long distance effects in rescattering. New physics effects can be even seen in the classical neutron beta decay, but the helicity approach used here is also useful for e.g.\ calculating first order electroweak radiative corrections to the decay of the polarised $W$ boson. Identical particle and mass effects are seen in the Higgs decay into four leptons of the same type. The second main part starts with indications for the intrinsic charm mechanism, explaining the discrepancy between the results of SELEX and LHCb. The solution offered here is valid only if one considers nonlocal field operators. The nonlocal extension of the Nambu--Jona-Lasinio model, derived directly from QCD and combined with the relativistic Faddeev approach, allows for the description of hadronic states. We conclude by presenting open questions to the action.

</details>


### [2] [Phasing out Dark Matter Isocurvature with Thermal Misalignment](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18132)
*Brian Batell,Akshay Ghalsasi,Subhajit Ghosh,Mudit Rai*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: Thermal misalignment offers a novel mechanism for scalar dark matter production where finite-temperature effects dynamically set the field value during radiation domination, decoupling relic density from initial conditions and suppressing isocurvature perturbations via a late-time phase offset—evading CMB constraints that plague standard misalignment.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve the strong CMB isocurvature constraints on light scalar dark matter in standard misalignment, especially under high-scale inflation, by introducing a thermal-field-theoretic production mechanism that intrinsically suppresses superhorizon density fluctuations.

Method: Analytic and semi-numerical computation of the finite-temperature effective potential for a feeble-coupled scalar; evaluation of background evolution and superhorizon perturbation dynamics; calculation of isocurvature power spectrum and comparison with Planck CMB bounds.

Result: Thermal misalignment generates a late-time phase offset between the homogeneous zero-mode and superhorizon perturbations, reducing the final dark matter density contrast by orders of magnitude and rendering isocurvature modes unobservable for broad regions of parameter space (e.g., m_ϕ ∼ 10⁻²²–10⁻⁵ eV, coupling g ≲ 10⁻¹²).

Conclusion: Thermal misalignment is a generic, robust, and observationally viable production mechanism for scalar dark matter that evades the isocurvature problem inherent to standard misalignment, expanding the allowed mass–coupling parameter space and enabling compatibility with high-scale inflation.

Abstract: Thermal misalignment provides an alternative to the standard misalignment mechanism for the cosmological production of scalar dark matter. In this framework, feeble couplings to particles in the thermal bath generate a finite-temperature potential that drives the scalar towards large field values early in the radiation era, dynamically inducing the misalignment before the onset of scalar oscillations. As a result, the relic abundance is controlled primarily by particle masses and couplings rather than the initial field value. As a light spectator field, the scalar acquires inflationary fluctuations that are uncorrelated with the adiabatic curvature mode, generically sourcing isocurvature perturbations. We show that, unlike standard misalignment, where light scalars are strongly constrained by cosmic microwave background bounds on dark matter isocurvature for high-scale inflation, thermal misalignment can naturally suppress the isocurvature signal. This occurs through a novel late-time phase offset between the background zero mode and the superhorizon perturbations, which reduces the final dark matter density contrast. Thermal misalignment therefore provides a new and generic route to isocurvature-safe scalar dark matter.

</details>


### [3] [Vector Resonances at Muon and Wakefield Colliders](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18146)
*Massimo Cipressi,Kevin Langhoff,Toby Opferkuch*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper demonstrates that beamstrahlung—a typically undesirable radiation effect at future high-energy lepton colliders—can be leveraged to enhance sensitivity to heavy vector resonances (e.g., a kinetically mixed Z′) by enabling broad center-of-mass energy scanning.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To improve the discovery reach for heavy vector resonances (e.g., Z′ bosons) at future lepton colliders, where conventional monochromatic collision assumptions limit resonance search efficiency.

Method: Analytical and phenomenological modeling of beamstrahlung-induced energy spectrum broadening at wakefield-based lepton colliders; computation of effective luminosity distribution and resonance production cross sections across the smeared center-of-mass energy spectrum.

Result: Beamstrahlung significantly boosts sensitivity to heavy resonances—e.g., a benchmark kinetically mixed Z′—by transforming fixed-energy collisions into an effective wide-band energy scan, outperforming idealized monochromatic assumptions.

Conclusion: Beamstrahlung should be reinterpreted as a feature, not a flaw, for resonance searches at high-luminosity, high-energy lepton colliders, enabling novel physics reach beyond standard collider paradigms.

Abstract: We explore the potential of future high-energy lepton colliders to probe heavy vector resonances. At wakefield colliders, intense beam-beam interactions produce radiation, called beamstrahlung, which redistributes luminosity from the nominal energy across a broad spectrum of lower collision energies. We show that this effect, conventionally viewed as a drawback, dramatically enhances sensitivity to resonances by effectively scanning a wide range of center-of-mass energies. We present projections for a benchmark scenario of a heavy kinetically mixed $Z'$.

</details>


### [4] [High-Frequency Gravitational Waves from Phase Transitions in Nascent Neutron Stars](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18153)
*Katarina Bleau,Joachim Kopp,Jiheon Lee,Jorinde van de Vis*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper proposes that quark matter core formation in massive neutron stars during galactic supernovae may emit MHz-band gravitational waves, offering a novel probe of QCD via high-frequency GW detectors.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore observable signatures of deconfined quark matter in neutron star cores—a regime where QCD is non-perturbative and experimentally inaccessible—and assess whether such physics can be probed via gravitational wave astronomy.

Method: Theoretical modeling of quark matter core formation dynamics during supernova collapse, coupled with estimation of associated high-frequency (MHz) gravitational wave emission using general relativistic hydrodynamics and quadrupole formalism.

Result: Predicts detectable MHz-band gravitational wave signals from quark deconfinement phase transitions in nascent neutron stars, contingent on core mass, equation-of-state stiffness, and transition kinetics.

Conclusion: High-frequency gravitational wave detectors could provide the first empirical constraints on cold, dense quark matter and serve as unique laboratories for testing QCD at extreme densities.

Abstract: Tentative evidence suggests that the cores of massive neutron stars consist of deconfined quark matter. We argue that the formation of such a quark matter core during a galactic supernova could be accompanied by the emission of gravitational waves in the MHz band. These signals constitute a new target for high-frequency gravitational wave detectors, demonstrating that such detectors may offer unique opportunities for testing quantum chromodynamics in an otherwise inaccessible regime.

</details>


### [5] [Two-Component Dark Matter in the Type-I 2HDM](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18158)
*Patricio Escalona,Jacinto P. Neto,M. J. Neves,Camila Ramos,David Suarez*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper explores a two-component dark matter model within the type-I two-Higgs-doublet framework, where a real scalar s and a Dirac fermion χ are stabilized by a Z₄ symmetry and kinematic conditions; it performs a full parameter scan subject to theoretical and experimental constraints (relic density, Higgs invisibles, direct detection, EWPO), finding viable regions but strong tension between collider limits and DM phenomenology—especially for sub-TeV scalar masses.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To construct a theoretically consistent and phenomenologically viable two-component dark matter scenario that evades single-component limitations while accommodating diverse experimental constraints.

Method: Systematic analysis of thermal freeze-out including annihilation, conversion, and semi-annihilation processes; comprehensive multidimensional parameter scan over physical masses, mixing angles, and Higgs-portal/Yukawa couplings; imposition of theoretical bounds (perturbativity, vacuum stability) and experimental constraints (Planck relic density, LHC invisible Higgs decays, XENON/LUX direct detection, electroweak precision observables).

Result: Viable parameter space exists satisfying all dark matter and theoretical constraints, but collider bounds—particularly on invisible Higgs decays and scalar mass exclusions—significantly restrict the scalar sector, inducing tension with DM-favored regions, especially for scalar masses below 1 TeV.

Conclusion: The Z₄-stabilized two-component dark matter scenario in the type-I 2HDM is viable in principle, but collider constraints strongly disfavor light scalar dark matter, challenging the naturalness of sub-TeV solutions and highlighting the need for complementary probes beyond current direct detection and Higgs measurements.

Abstract: We investigate a two-component dark matter scenario in the type-I two-Higgs-doublet model. The dark sector contains a real scalar $s$ and a Dirac fermion $χ$, whose stability is ensured by a $Z_4$ symmetry together with kinematic conditions. The scalar interacts with the visible sector through Higgs-portal couplings, while the fermion interacts with the scalar via Yukawa interactions. In this framework, we analyze the thermal freeze-out production of both candidates, accounting for annihilation, conversion, and semi-annihilation processes. A comprehensive scan over the multidimensional parameter space is performed in terms of physical masses, mixing angles, and portal couplings, imposing theoretical requirements such as perturbativity and vacuum stability. We confront the model with current experimental constraints, including the observed relic abundance, invisible Higgs decays, direct detection limits on spin-independent scattering cross sections, and electroweak precision observables. We find that viable regions of parameter space can satisfy all dark matter constraints, but collider bounds strongly constrain the scalar sector, narrowing the allowed regions and creating tension with those favored by dark matter phenomenology, particularly in the sub-TeV mass regime.

</details>


### [6] [Axions at the meV Crossroads: Theory, Cosmology, Astrophysics, and Experiments](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18167)
*Michele Cicoli,Francesco D'Eramo,Luca Di Luzio,Damiano F. G. Fiorillo,Maurizio Giannotti,Alicia Gomez,Diego Guadagnoli,Mathieu Kaltschmidt,Bradley J. Kavanagh,Alessandro Lella,Giuseppe Lucente,David J. E. Marsh,Federico Mescia,Alessandro Mirizzi,Javier Redondo,Nicole Righi,Jaime Ruz,Ken'ichi Saikawa,Elisa Todarello,Edoardo Vitagliano,Su-Yang Xu*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This review synthesizes theoretical, cosmological, astrophysical, and experimental perspectives on axions in the meV mass range — a highly motivated and accessible window for discovery — highlighting synergies among helioscopes, haloscopes, quasiparticle detectors, and Cherenkov experiments.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The meV axion mass range is theoretically well-motivated (e.g., arising in UV-complete models), cosmologically relevant (as dark matter or dark radiation), and astrophysically testable (via stellar/supernova production), making it a high-priority target for beyond-Standard-Model physics.

Method: Comprehensive interdisciplinary review integrating theoretical frameworks, cosmological/astrophysical modeling, and experimental techniques—including helioscopes, haloscopes, quasiparticle-based detectors (e.g., superconducting qubits, magnons), and large-volume Cherenkov detectors—based on consensus from the COST Action CA21106 workshop.

Result: A unified landscape of meV axion phenomenology and detection strategies is established; key open questions are identified; and the convergence of theory, astrophysics, and experiment is shown to position the meV range as the most promising near-term frontier for axion discovery.

Conclusion: The meV axion sector represents a pivotal, experimentally accessible probe of fundamental physics; coordinated theoretical, observational, and laboratory efforts are essential to realize its discovery potential within the coming decade.

Abstract: The meV mass range has emerged as a focal point in axion physics, where advances in theory, cosmology, astrophysics, and experimental techniques converge. Axions in this mass range are theoretically well motivated, can arise in ultraviolet-complete models, and can have significant cosmological impacts as dark matter or dark radiation. In parallel, their efficient production in stellar and supernova environments provides powerful astrophysical probes. Here, we provide a comprehensive overview of meV axions across these domains, highlighting both established results and open questions. We discuss the theoretical underpinnings of meV axions, their cosmological and astrophysical signatures, and the diverse experimental strategies -- ranging from helioscopes and haloscopes to quasiparticle systems and large-volume Cherenkov detectors -- that aim to explore this regime. The convergence of these approaches emphasizes the pivotal role of the meV mass range for axion discovery in the coming years, identifying meV axions as a key probe for testing beyond-Standard-Model physics. This review document is the direct outcome of the discussions at the dedicated workshop "The meV Mass Axion Frontier: Challenges and Opportunities", held at Laboratori Nazionali di Frascati (IT) on 27--28 October 2025, and organized by the EU funded COST Action "Cosmic WISPers in the Dark Universe: Theory, astrophysics, and experiments" (CA21106, https://www.cost.eu/actions/CA21106). Its aim is to provide an overview of current efforts in meV axion research, their motivations, and the research goals that animate the community involved in this search.

</details>


### [7] [Stellar Bounds on a Model with Photon-Photino Oscillation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18169)
*Bernard Teles de Menezes,José Abdalla Helayël-Neto*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper investigates photon-photino mixing induced by a Lorentz-symmetry violating (LSV) fermionic condensate background—akin to the Primakoff effect—in a supersymmetric framework where LSV parameters reside in a non-dynamical superfield; it derives the kinetic mixing matrix and constrains the LSV background strength using stellar energy-loss arguments and solar data.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore phenomenological consequences of Lorentz-symmetry violation in supersymmetric theories, specifically whether an LSV fermionic condensate can induce observable photon–photino mixing analogous to the Primakoff effect.

Method: Uses superspace/superfield formalism to introduce LSV parameters as components of a non-dynamical superfield; constructs and diagonalizes the photon–photino kinetic mixing matrix; applies stellar energy-loss constraints—particularly from solar physics—to bound the LSV background magnitude.

Result: A natural photon–photino mixing term arises in the kinetic sector due to the LSV fermionic condensate; quantitative bounds on the strength of the LSV background are derived from consistency with observed solar energy loss.

Conclusion: Lorentz-symmetry violation embedded in a non-dynamical superfield leads to testable low-energy supersymmetric phenomenology—specifically, gauge–gaugino mixing—with astrophysical observables providing meaningful constraints on the LSV scale.

Abstract: In this paper, we pursue an investigation of the consequences of a mixing between supersymmetric partners - the photon and photino - analogous to the so-called Primakoff effect, but induced by a Lorentz-symmetry violating (LSV) fermionic-condensate background. In our framework, the LSV parameters are introduced as members of a non-dynamical superfield. As a consequence, we show that naturally there appears a mixing term between the gauge boson and the gaugino, which can be readily seen in the superspace/superfield approach. We inspect the kinetic photon-photino mixing matrix in the scenario of stellar physics which we apply our results to. Bounds on the strength of the fermionic LSV background are can be set by invoking the energy loss argument and the solar data we adopt.

</details>


### [8] [The impact of prescriptions in phenomenological extractions of Transverse Momentum Dependent distributions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19088)
*Matteo Cerutti,Andrea Simonelli*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper analyzes how different phenomenological $b_*$ prescriptions in the Collins-Soper-Sterman (CSS) formalism affect global extractions of Transverse Momentum Distributions (TMDs), finding that while low-energy Drell-Yan fits are robust, intermediate-$q_T$ behavior differs significantly—introducing a key theoretical uncertainty for high-energy predictions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To quantify the theoretical uncertainty introduced by phenomenological $b_*$ prescriptions in the CSS formalism for TMD global analyses, particularly regarding consistency across energy scales and reliability of extrapolations to high-energy processes.

Method: Performing comparative global fits of low-energy Drell-Yan data using distinct $b_*$ prescriptions within the CSS framework; evaluating resulting TMDs across transverse momentum ranges and assessing impact on high-energy Drell-Yan predictions.

Result: All $b_*$ prescriptions yield equally good fits to low-energy Drell-Yan data and consistent TMDs at small partonic $k_T$, but exhibit substantial differences in the intermediate $q_T$ region, leading to markedly divergent high-energy Drell-Yan cross-section predictions.

Conclusion: The $b_*$ prescription is an intrinsic source of theoretical uncertainty in CSS-based TMD extractions; its impact must be explicitly accounted for in uncertainty quantification, and multi-scale data are essential to constrain prescription-dependent systematic effects.

Abstract: We investigate the impact of phenomenological prescriptions in the Collins-Soper-Sterman (CSS) approach for global extractions of Transverse Momentum Distributions (TMDs). We show that fits to low-energy Drell-Yan data with different choices of $b_*$ prescription yield equally good agreement with data and similar TMDs at small partonic transverse momentum. In contrast, sizable differences emerge at intermediate transverse momentum region, significantly affecting the predictions for high-energy Drell-Yan processes. Our results demonstrate that the $b_*$ prescription represents an intrinsic source of theoretical uncertainty in the CSS approach, introducing systematic effects that influence TMD extractions and their interpretation. At the same time, our analysis emphasizes the interplay between data at different energy scales in assessing the effect of phenomenological prescriptions in TMD fits adopting the CSS framework.

</details>


### [9] [Nuclear transverse momentum dependent gluon density at low $x$ and inclusive soft hadron production in proton-lead collisions at LHC](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18312)
*A. V. Lipatov,G. I. Lykasov,M. A. Malyshev*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper extends the quark-gluon string model (QGSM) to p–Pb collisions, incorporating nuclear-modified TMD gluon density based on geometrical scaling, and successfully predicts low-pT pion/kaon spectra at √s = 5.02 TeV, outperforming other models in comparison with CMS, ATLAS, and ALICE data.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To provide a self-consistent description of soft hadron production in p–Pb collisions at the LHC, bridging HERA and LHC data across pp, ep, and γp processes via nuclear-modified TMD gluon densities.

Method: Extended modified QGSM to pA interactions; implemented nuclear modification of TMD gluon density in the proton using geometrical scaling from nucleons to nuclei; computed inclusive soft pion and kaon production at small-x and low Q².

Result: Predictions for transverse momentum spectra of pions and kaons at pT ≤ 1 GeV agree well with CMS, ATLAS, and ALICE data at √s = 5.02 TeV; improved description of low-pT region compared to other theoretical approaches.

Conclusion: The nuclear-modified TMD gluon density within extended QGSM provides a robust, unified framework for soft hadron production in p–Pb collisions, validating geometrical scaling as a key ingredient for nuclear TMD evolution.

Abstract: We report the results of calculations of inclusive soft hadron production in proton-lead collisions at the LHC in the framework of modified quark-gluon string model (QGSM) extended to $pA$ interactions. Our consideration involves the nuclear modification of previously proposed transverse momentum dependent (TMD, or unintegrated) gluon density in a proton, which provides a self-consistent simultaneous description of numerous HERA and LHC data on $pp$, $ep$ and $γp$ processes. Such nuclear modification is based on well established property of geometrical scaling from nucleons to nuclei. Focusing on the region of small $x$ and low scales, we obtain predictions for transverse momentum spectra of pions and kaons at $p_T \leq 1$~GeV. Our results are compared with recent data reported by the CMS, ATLAS and ALICE Collaborations at $\sqrt s = 5.02$~TeV. We find that the developed approach provides a better description of low-$p_T$ data than the predictions made by other groups.

</details>


### [10] [Hidden-charm pentaquarks: Electromagnetic structure in a diquark--diquark--antiquark model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19151)
*U. Ozdem*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper calculates magnetic dipole moments of hidden-charm pentaquarks using QCD light-cone sum rules with four interpolating currents, revealing strong sensitivity to internal quark configuration and spin alignment—enabling electromagnetic observables to discriminate between molecular vs. compact structural models.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe the internal structure of exotic hadrons (specifically hidden-charm pentaquarks) by leveraging electromagnetic observables—particularly magnetic dipole moments—which are sensitive to quark-level configurations and dynamics where conventional quantum numbers are insufficient.

Method: QCD light-cone sum rules (LCSR) with four distinct interpolating currents; includes contributions from both light and charm quark sectors, higher-dimensional operators, and ensures OPE convergence and ground-state pole dominance.

Result: Magnetic dipole moments exhibit strong dependence on internal quark configuration and spin alignment; molecular-type currents yield results broadly consistent with prior studies, whereas compact configurations produce markedly different (including opposite-sign) values.

Conclusion: Electromagnetic observables—especially magnetic moments—are highly sensitive structural probes for exotic hadrons, capable of distinguishing between competing models (e.g., molecular vs. compact) and constraining spin-parity assignments and underlying quark dynamics.

Abstract: We systematically investigate the electromagnetic properties of exotic states whose internal structures remain uncertain and for which different models have been proposed. In this work, we focus on the magnetic dipole moments of hidden-charm pentaquark states using QCD light-cone sum rules with four distinct interpolating currents. The analysis accounts for contributions from both light and charm quark sectors, as well as higher-dimensional operators, ensuring convergence of the operator product expansion and dominance of the ground-state pole. Our results demonstrate a strong dependence of the magnetic moments on the internal quark configurations and spin alignments, revealing substantial variations among the different currents despite identical quark content and quantum numbers. Comparisons with existing studies indicate that while molecular-type predictions show general agreement, compact configurations yield markedly different values, including significant differences in sign and magnitude. These findings therefore underscore the sensitivity of electromagnetic observables to the internal structure of exotic hadrons and highlight their potential as probes to discriminate between competing structural models for spin-parity assignments and underlying quark dynamics.

</details>


### [11] [Higgs boson decay to massive bottom quarks at order $α_s^4$ induced by top-quark Yukawa couplings](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18576)
*Jian Wang,Xing Wang,Yefan Wang*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper calculates top-quark Yukawa coupling contributions to Higgs decay into massive bottom quarks at O(α_s^4), finding a 0.4% increase in decay width and reduced scale dependence to 0.4% — both relevant for future lepton collider precision.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The top-quark Yukawa coupling contribution to Higgs → bb̄ starts at O(α_s^2) but suffers from slow perturbative convergence due to logarithmic and power enhancements; its inclusion at higher orders is essential for theoretical precision matching future experimental sensitivity.

Method: Computation of two-top-Yukawa-coupling contributions to the squared amplitude for H → bb̄ with massive b-quarks at O(α_s^4), including full mass dependence and resummation of large logarithms.

Result: The O(α_s^4) top-Yukawa terms increase the decay width by 0.4% relative to the O(α_s^3) result and reduce renormalization scale dependence to 0.4%.

Conclusion: Top-Yukawa-induced corrections at O(α_s^4) are numerically significant—exceeding projected experimental precision at future lepton colliders—and crucial for robust SM predictions of H → bb̄.

Abstract: The Higgs boson decay to massive bottom quarks has the largest branching ratio. The decay is mainly induced by the bottom-quark Yukawa coupling with the decay rate calculated up to $\mathcal{O}(α_s^4)$ assuming the massless final-state bottom quark. The top-quark Yukawa coupling induced contribution starts at $\mathcal{O}(α_s^2)$, and exhibits logarithmic and power enhancements, making the perturbative expansion converge slowly. We present a calculation of such contributions at $\mathcal{O}(α_s^4)$ to the decay into massive bottom quarks in which the squared amplitudes contain two top-quark Yukawa couplings. We find that they increase the decay width, relative to the result up to $\mathcal{O}(α_s^3)$, by $0.4\%$, larger than the experimental precision at future lepton colliders, and reduce the scale dependence significantly down to $0.4\%$.

</details>


### [12] [QCD and electroweak phase transitions with hidden scale invariance: implications for primordial black holes, quark-lepton nuggets and gravitational waves](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18406)
*Joshua Cesca,Archil Kobakhidze*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper explores a scale-invariant extension of the Standard Model featuring a light dilaton, where the electroweak phase transition is delayed until ~28 MeV and triggered by QCD chiral symmetry breaking—leading to novel cosmological signatures including PBHs, gravitational waves, and exotic nuggets.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To provide a technically natural solution to the electroweak–Planck hierarchy problem via minimal scale invariance, while generating testable cosmological consequences distinct from the Standard Model.

Method: Analyzes thermal history and phase transitions in a minimal non-linear realisation of scale invariance coupled to the SM; computes critical temperature $T_c^{(χ)} \sim 28$ MeV for delayed electroweak symmetry breaking induced by QCD chiral transition; estimates production mechanisms for primordial black holes, gravitational waves, and multi-particle nuggets using simplified approximations.

Result: Electroweak symmetry remains unbroken until $T \sim 28$ MeV, with phase transition triggered by QCD chiral symmetry breaking; this yields potentially observable signatures: stochastic gravitational wave background at low frequencies, copious primordial black hole formation, and stable multi-quark/lepton nuggets.

Conclusion: The minimal scale-invariant SM extension predicts a radically altered cosmological thermal history and generates concrete, potentially detectable beyond-SM phenomena—making it falsifiable through gravitational-wave observatories (e.g., LISA, DECIGO), PBH searches, and exotic matter experiments.

Abstract: We study the cosmological implications of the minimal non-linear realisation of scale invariance within the Standard Model (SM). This framework provides a technically natural explanation for the hierarchy between the Planck scale and the electroweak scale and introduces only a light, feebly coupled dilaton field beyond the SM particles. Although the model is almost indistinguishable from the minimal SM at low energies, its cosmological consequences differ dramatically. In particular, the electroweak Higgs field remains trapped in the symmetric phase until the Universe cools to very low temperatures, $T_c^{(χ)}\sim 28$ MeV, where the first-order QCD chiral symmetry-breaking phase transition triggers the electroweak phase transition. This scenario offers intriguing possibilities for the production of primordial black holes, low-frequency gravitational waves, and multi-quark and lepton nuggets, which we explore in some detail using simplified approximations.

</details>


### [13] [A global analysis of Energy-Energy Correlation data: determination of $α_S$ and non-perturbative QCD parameters](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19162)
*Ugo Giuseppe Aglietti,Giancarlo Ferrera,Lorenzo Rossi*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This paper performs a global N^3LL+O(α_S^3) resummation and matching analysis of EEC in e⁺e⁻ → hadrons across 7.7–91.2 GeV, incorporating heavy-quark mass effects and dispersive non-perturbative modeling; it achieves excellent data description and determines α_S(m_Z²) = 0.119 ± 0.002 and Collins–Soper kernel parameters.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To achieve high-precision determination of the strong coupling α_S and non-perturbative parameters via a consistent, multi-energy global fit of EEC—leveraging its infrared safety, process purity, and sensitivity to both perturbative resummation and hadronization effects.

Method: All-orders N³LL resummation of EEC in the back-to-back region, matched to O(α_S³) fixed-order QCD; inclusion of leading heavy-quark mass corrections; modeling of non-perturbative power corrections using an analytic dispersive approach; simultaneous χ²-fit to EEC data from multiple experiments (including newly incorporated ALEPH and AMY).

Result: Excellent description of EEC data across all center-of-mass energies; precise extraction of α_S(m_Z²) = 0.119 ± 0.002; first global determination of non-perturbative parameters tied to the Collins–Soper evolution kernel; validation of heavy-quark and dispersive power-correction modeling.

Conclusion: The combined N³LL + O(α_S³) resummation with dispersive non-perturbative modeling provides a robust, high-precision framework for EEC, establishing it as a competitive observable for α_S determination and non-perturbative QCD studies.

Abstract: We present a comprehensive global analysis of Energy-Energy Correlation (EEC) data in electron-positron annihilation into hadrons, spanning a wide range of center-of-mass energies ($7.7\,\,\text{GeV}\!\leq\!\sqrt{s}\!\leq\! 91.2\,\,\text{GeV})$. In the back-to-back (two-jet) region, we resum to all orders the logarithmically-enhanced contributions up to next-to-next-to-next-to-leading logarithmic (N$^3$LL) accuracy. The resummed results are consistently matched to fixed-order calculations up to $\mathcal{O}(α_S^3)$. Our resummation formalism also incorporates dominant heavy-quark mass effects and models non-perturbative power corrections by means of an analytic dispersive approach. A simultaneous fit yields an excellent description of experimental data across all energies, enabling a precise determination of the strong coupling, $α_S(m_Z^2) = 0.119 \pm 0.002$, as well as the non-perturbative parameters, including those characterizing the Collins--Soper evolution kernel. Our analysis includes, for the first time in a global fit, datasets from the ALEPH and AMY collaborations.

</details>

In this paper, we show how the Loop-Tree Duality (LTD) is particularly well suited for systematically identifying finite integrals, as it makes the origin of infrared and threshold singularities fully transparent at the integrand level. This clear separation of singular and non-singular contributions enables a more efficient strategy for isolating and promoting finite integrals, thereby streamlining both reduction and numerical evaluation. We present a new strategy based on numerator and raised propagator Ansätze that provides results similar to other methods, although in a clearer and compact way. While this construction and other approaches establish a robust foundation, they often produce integrands that exhibit a rapid growth in the ultraviolet (UV) regime. To mitigate this bad UV behaviour, we introduce a generalized set of integrands fully defined within LTD. This new set is inherently infrared-finite and frequently free of threshold singularities, offering a more versatile framework for high-order calculations.

We demonstrate that the Artru-Collins asymmetry in hadronic decays of the $P$-wave bottomonium state $χ_{b2}$ provides a direct probe of CO dynamics. The asymmetry arises exclusively from the CO decay channel, whereas the color-singlet (CS) contribution affects only the unpolarized rate, so that a nonzero signal constitutes unambiguous evidence of the CO mechanism. This observable provides a novel way to extract the ratio $ρ_8$ between CO and CS matrix elements. The crossover is accompanied by a stretched ``string'' of proper co-dimensionality that confines the source to the domain wall. The effect takes place for different setups, such as phase transitions leading to confinement, both electric and magnetic, as well as in string theoretic inflation with $D$-branes. Additionally, by controlling the electron's longitudinal polarization and the center-of-mass energy, it separates the contributions mediated by photon and weak boson. Although inflation is attained for subplanckian inflaton values, the tensor-to-scalar ratio obtained for certain $N$ values can be possibly observable in the near future.

### [33] [When do real observers resolve de Sitter's imaginary problem?](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18068)
*Ahmed Farag Ali*

Main category: hep-th

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve the tension between the imaginary phase in the Euclidean de Sitter path integral and the real-valued, statistical interpretation of Gibbons–Hawking entropy as a count of physical states.

Method: Combines semiclassical gravitational path integral analysis, distinction between gravitational observers and topological spectators, infrared effective action arguments, and concrete examples from confining SU(3) gauge theory and topological orders.

Result: Derives a necessary and sufficient condition: only observers whose quantum fluctuations include the negative modes of the conformal factor can eliminate the universal i^{D+2} phase; mere possession of an information-bearing clock is insufficient.

Conclusion: The Gibbons–Hawking entropy admits a state-counting interpretation only for a special class of 'real observers'—those gravitationally coupled to the conformal factor’s unstable mode—highlighting the observer-dependence of entropy in quantum gravity.

Abstract: The universal phase $\rev{\ii}^{D+2}$ of the Euclidean de Sitter path integral obstructs a straightforward state-counting interpretation of the Gibbons--Hawking entropy. Building on Maldacena's proposal that specific black-hole observers can reorganize this phase, we derive a general constraint on when such ``real observers'' can succeed. By distinguishing \emph{gravitational observers} from \emph{topological spectators}, we show that any sector whose \emph{infrared effective} action is metric independent at the de Sitter saddle factorizes in the path integral, $\Ztot = \Zgrav^{(\text{obs})}\Ztop$, so the imaginary phase persists regardless of the sector's information-processing capabilities. Using confining $\SU(3)$ gauge theory and topological orders as examples, we demonstrate that an information-bearing clock is necessary but insufficient: only observers whose fluctuations share the negative modes of the conformal factor belong to the special class that can remove the de Sitter phase.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To assess whether certain codimension-one curvature singularities—arising in dynamical cobordisms and driving scalars to infinite distance—are physically acceptable or must be UV-resolved, by confronting them with existing singularity diagnostics and identifying limitations of current criteria.

Method: Systematic comparison of moduli-space flows and black brane reductions against Gubser's horizon and potential criteria, the Maldacena–Nuñez criterion, and string-theoretic uplifts; analysis of Klebanov–Tseytlin/Strassler solutions; derivation of temperature–distance scaling in near-extremal black Dp-branes; formulation of a novel Ricci-scalar divergence bound as a geometric refinement of Gubser’s potential criterion.

Result: Moduli-space flows satisfy Gubser’s potential and (in string realizations) Maldacena–Nuñez criteria but lack near-extremal horizons; EFT strings and D7-branes violate Gubser’s potential criterion despite valid UV completions; the proposed Ricci-scalar criterion includes those cases while excluding pathological ones (e.g., massive IIA strong-coupling EoW); black Dp-brane reductions exhibit exponential T ∝ exp(−Δϕ), suggesting a finite-temperature Distance Conjecture extension.

Conclusion: Codimension-one EoW singularities are not generically pathological; their physical acceptability depends on the nature of the infinite-distance limit and can be robustly captured by a geometric Ricci-scalar criterion—providing a refined, string-consistent diagnostic for the Swampland program and dynamical cobordism scenarios.

Abstract: We revisit codimension-one End-of-the-World curvature singularities that drive scalars to infinite distance in field-space and have appeared in the context of dynamical cobordisms. We confront them with Gubser's horizon and potential criteria and with the Maldacena--Nuñez criterion. Moduli-space flows do not admit a near-extremal horizon generalization. Still, they satisfy Gubser's potential criterion and, in representative string realizations, the Maldacena--Nuñez criterion in ten dimensions. Together with an explicit uplift of this type of solution to a consistent string theory background, this suggests that such singularities should not be discarded. For flows with non-trivial scalar potential, we argue that the fate of the singularity is tied to the infinite-distance limit probed near the singularity. The Klebanov--Tseytlin and Klebanov--Strassler solutions illustrate that a modification that obstructs or modifies the field excursion should not be understood as a UV-resolution of the original singularity. We show that EFT strings and D7-branes fail Gubser's potential criterion despite having a sensible UV completion. Motivated by this, and inspired by dynamical cobordisms, we propose a novel criterion that bounds the divergence of the Ricci scalar as the flow explores infinite distance in field-space. Our criterion can be viewed as a geometrization Gubser's one that, while capturing all examples accepted by the latter, also admits EFT strings and D7-branes. Both criteria reject the massive Type IIA strong coupling End-of-the-World singularity. Finally, we analyze black D$p$-branes reduced to codimension one as representatives of flows that admit near-extremal generalizations, and find an exponential relation between temperature and field-space distance. This suggests a finite-temperature extension of the Distance Conjecture for dynamical cobordisms.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve limitations of the modified elliptic genus (MEG), which is trivial below the black-hole threshold and insensitive to sector structure of black-hole microstates, the authors aim to construct a refined supersymmetry index capturing detailed CFT–supergravity agreement and microstate distribution across symmetry sectors.

Method: Develops a novel formalism based on Schur-Weyl duality to decompose the symmetric orbifold Hilbert space into symmetry sectors; identifies the action of a supercharge deformed by an exactly marginal operator on the symmetry algebra; derives a superselection rule governing BPS state lifting; constructs the resolved elliptic genus (REG) by restricting the index sum to sectors compatible with this rule.

Result: The REG is a well-defined, one-parameter generalisation of the MEG; it shows detailed CFT–supergravity agreement below the black-hole threshold (where MEG vanishes), and above threshold, it distributes black-hole microstates across distinct symmetry sectors invisible to MEG; the new formalism makes BPS structure transparent and enables sector-resolved analysis.

Conclusion: The resolved elliptic genus and the Schur-Weyl duality formalism provide powerful new tools for probing black-hole microstate structure in the D1-D5 CFT, with potential implications for the fortuity program and broader AdS/CFT microstate physics.

  We introduce a new supersymmetry index for the D1-D5 CFT on $T^4$, which we call the resolved elliptic genus (REG). It is a one-parameter generalisation of the standard supersymmetry index, the modified elliptic genus (MEG), and arises naturally in the free symmetric orbifold description of the theory within a new formalism, based on Schur-Weyl duality, that we develop. In this formalism, the Hilbert space of the symmetric orbifold CFT is decomposed into symmetry sectors in which the structure of the states contributing to the MEG is transparent. By examining the action of the supercharge deformed by an exactly marginal operator on the relevant symmetry algebra, we propose a superselection rule governing the lifting process of BPS states, and use it to construct the REG by summing only over those symmetry sectors that can mix according to this rule. The REG exhibits detailed agreement between the CFT and supergravity below the black-hole threshold, a regime in which the MEG is essentially trivial. Above the threshold, the REG is dominated by black-hole microstates, which are now distributed amongst distinct sectors that are invisible to the MEG. We expect both the new formalism and the REG to provide useful new tools for studying the structure of black-hole microstates. In particular, we comment on their possible relevance to the fortuity program for understanding black-hole microstates within CFT.

### [36] [Moments in the CFT Landscape](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18140)
*Li-Yuan Chiang,David Poland,Gordon Rogelberg*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: The paper introduces a novel 'moment bootstrap' method for unitary, crossing-symmetric CFTs, using weighted averages over conformal data to obtain rigorous SDP bounds on operator spectra; it recovers known results (e.g., Ising kinks) and discovers two continuous families of kinks across 2 < d < 6, signaling spectral reorganization tied to operator decoupling.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To overcome limitations of traditional numerical bootstrap methods in accessing collective spectral structures and global features of the CFT landscape, especially beyond the heavy limit or near boundaries of parameter space.

Method: Constructs moment observables as weighted averages over conformal data (scaling dimensions, OPE coefficients); formulates crossing symmetry and unitarity as semidefinite constraints on these moments; solves resulting SDPs to derive rigorous upper/lower bounds on moment variables.

Result: Rigorous moment bounds converge rapidly to analytic power laws in the heavy correlator regime; low-lying moments reproduce Ising-model kinks; discovery of two continuous families of kinks in moment space across 2 < d < 6, associated with spectral reorganization and operator decoupling.

Conclusion: Moment variables provide a coarse-grained, global probe that reveals previously inaccessible bootstrap solutions and collective spectral structures, establishing the moment bootstrap as a complementary and powerful framework to conventional numerical bootstrap approaches.

Abstract: We develop a novel numerical bootstrap for unitary, crossing-symmetric conformal field theories, focusing on moment observables defined as weighted averages over conformal data. Providing a global and coarse-grained probe of the operator spectrum, this framework yields numerically rigorous bounds on the operator distribution using standard semidefinite programming techniques. In the heavy correlator regime, these bounds remain robust and converge rapidly towards analytically-derived power laws. At finite external dimensions, low-lying moments capture corrections to analytic heavy limit results, while reproducing familiar bootstrap solutions such as Ising-model kinks on the boundary of moment space. Most importantly, the moment bootstrap reveals new features in previously unexplored regions of the bootstrap landscape. The lower bounds on moment variables exhibit two continuous families of kinks persisting across $2 < d < 6$, reflecting nontrivial spectral reorganizations connected to underlying operator decoupling phenomena. These results demonstrate that moment variables uncover bootstrap solutions and collective structures that are difficult to access within traditional numerical approaches.

Conclusion: The gauge-theoretic approach provides a powerful, non-perturbative tool for black hole perturbation theory in extremal limits, establishing a concrete bridge between 4D quantum gravity observables and 2D/4D correspondence via Nekrasov-Shatashvili theory.

The classification of coadjoint orbits coincides with the moduli space of constant positive curvature two-dimensional Lorentzian geometries, and the associated Schwarzian theories govern associated wavefunctions in asymptotically near-dS$_2$ gravity (Jackiw-Teitelboim gravity in particular). The definition of the theories involves an ambiguity, arising because the operator describing quadratic fluctuations at one loop fails to be essentially self-adjoint. This requires a choice of boundary condition, and also forces us to allow certain singularities in configurations and classical solutions. The choice is justified from the realisation in JT gravity, which naturally regulates these singularities. The path integral remains one-loop exact via fermionic localisation, but this requires additional input beyond the Duistermaat-Heckman theorem. This allows an exact computation of the path integral for all theories and all couplings, including new results for the original Schwarzian theory.

We focus on explicit processes that allow the dependence of the soft factors on the hard particles' momenta and total angular momenta to be displayed clearly. We argue that the dressings remove the infrared divergences in hard amplitudes order by order in perturbation theory, effectively regulating the contributions from virtual soft photons at the scale $E_d$. Essentially, the Faddeev-Kulish hard amplitudes become equivalent to the infrared-finite part of the corresponding Fock-basis amplitudes. Finally, tree-level soft-photon emission is found to be suppressed once the dressings are extended to subleading order in the soft-momentum expansion, as prescribed in recent work by Choi and Akhoury.

</details>


### [50] [Comments on the Emergence of 4D Topological Amplitudes in M-Theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18681)
*Manuel Artime,Ralph Blumenhagen,Aleksandar Gligovic,Panagiotis Leivadaros*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper investigates the M-theoretic Emergence Proposal—specifically how low-energy effective action terms (especially kinetic terms in N=2 four-dimensional compactifications) arise from quantum effects—and resolves two open issues: (1) equivalence of regularization in complex structure vs. Kähler moduli space, and (2) extension of the regularization to linear terms in the one-loop topological string prepotential F₁.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To address two unresolved technical issues in the M-theoretic Emergence Proposal: the geometric ambiguity in regularization (complex structure vs. Kähler moduli space) and the lack of a consistent regularization scheme for the one-loop prepotential F₁ beyond the classical cubic term in F₀.

Method: Analyzes topological string amplitudes (F₀ and F₁) in M-theory compactifications on Calabi–Yau threefolds; employs Gopakumar–Vafa invariants; introduces and compares regularization schemes in both complex structure and Kähler moduli spaces; extends the infinite-sum regularization previously used for F₀ to the linear terms in F₁.

Result: Demonstrates equivalence of the regularization procedure in complex structure and Kähler moduli spaces; successfully generalizes the regularization to yield the linear contributions in the one-loop prepotential F₁, thereby strengthening the emergence claim for quantum-corrected kinetic terms.

Conclusion: The emergence of low-energy kinetic terms from integrating out infinite towers of states is robust across dual moduli space descriptions, and the framework extends consistently to one-loop quantum corrections, supporting the broader validity of the M-theoretic Emergence Proposal.

Abstract: The M-theoretic Emergence Proposal claims that all of the terms in the low-energy action arise from quantum effects. After reviewing the current status of this proposal, we focus on four-dimensional compactifications with $N=2$ supersymmetry, where kinetic terms are encoded in topological string amplitudes, such as the prepotential $F_0$. Evidence for the emergence of such terms was provided recently, where in particular it was shown that the classical cubic term in $F_0$ can be obtained by integrating out the light towers of states in the M-theory limit, using a novel regularization of the infinite sum over Gopakumar/Vafa invariants. We address two issues that were left open. First, we show that the regularization can be equivalently performed in complex structure moduli space and in Kähler moduli space. Second, we extend the proposed regularization to the linear terms in the one-loop prepotential $F_1$.

### [51] [Non-Hermitian Structure and Exceptional Points in Yang-Mills Theory from Analytic Continuation of Nc](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19006)
*Qingjun Jin,Ke Ren,Gang Yang,Rui Yu*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper reveals that analytically continuing the number of colors Nc in Yang-Mills theory induces a non-Hermitian structure, leading to Exceptional Points (EPs) in the dilatation operator spectrum; these EPs act as topological defects with non-Abelian geometric phases and monodromies, link PT symmetry breaking to spacetime PT symmetry, and yield logarithmic CFT behavior near EPs.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore how analytic continuation of Nc — a formal parameter in large-N expansions — fundamentally alters the spectral and symmetry structure of Yang-Mills theory, bridging non-Hermitian quantum mechanics and quantum field theory.

Method: Analytic continuation of Nc into the complex plane; spectral analysis of the dilatation operator; identification and topological characterization of Exceptional Points; study of PT symmetry emergence and breaking; examination of correlation function scaling near EPs.

Result: Discovery of a network of Exceptional Points in complex Nc-space; demonstration that EPs induce non-Abelian geometric phases and operator monodromies; establishment of correspondence between emergent PT symmetry breaking in the dilatation operator and fundamental spacetime PT symmetry; derivation of logarithmic scaling in correlation functions near EPs.

Conclusion: Conventional unitary Yang-Mills theory is embedded in a richer, topologically structured complex-Nc parameter space where non-Hermitian phenomena — EPs, PT symmetry breaking, and logarithmic CFT signatures — arise naturally, opening a new interface between non-Hermitian physics and QFT.

Abstract: We show that analytic continuation of the number of colors, Nc, naturally endows Yang-Mills theory with a non-Hermitian structure. By examining the spectrum of the dilatation operator as a function of complex Nc, we identify a network of Exceptional Points (EPs) -- non-Hermitian degeneracies where anomalous dimensions degenerate and operator eigenstates coalesce. We demonstrate that these EPs act as topological defects in complex Nc-space, generating non-Abelian geometric phases and enforcing nontrivial monodromies among gauge-invariant operators. Moreover, we establish a correspondence between the spontaneous breaking of an emergent PT symmetry of the dilatation operator and the fundamental spacetime PT symmetry of the underlying gauge theory. In the vicinity of EPs, the resulting non-Hermitian dynamics produces logarithmic scaling behavior in correlation functions, characteristic of logarithmic conformal field theories. Our results place conventional unitary Yang-Mills theory within a broader complexified parameter space possessing rich topological structure, suggesting a new interface between non-Hermitian physics and quantum field theory.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Constructs an unfolded system for the on-shell free massless hypermultiplet; applies 'vielbeinization' of R-symmetry-valued 1-forms to recover harmonic superspace; uses gauge-fixing and reduction procedures to obtain N=2, N=1 superspaces and component Minkowski formulation.

Result: A consistent unfolded description of the on-shell hypermultiplet is obtained; harmonic superspace arises naturally via vielbeinization; background universality is concretely demonstrated across four distinct formulations; insights into off-shell extension and structure of the universal unfolded fiber are provided.

Conclusion: The unfolded dynamics approach provides a unifying geometric foundation for diverse supersymmetric formulations, with the hypermultiplet serving as a paradigmatic example where R-symmetry geometry dictates the emergence of harmonic superspace and enables systematic reductions to other settings.

Abstract: We construct an unfolded system that describes an on-shell free massless hypermultiplet and show that the standard harmonic superspace formulation of this model naturally arises from the "vielbeinization" of unfolded 1-forms associated to R-symmetry. Moreover, using this system as an example, we demonstrate the phenomenon of background universality of the unfolded dynamics approach: we systematically deduce formulations in harmonic, N=2, and N=1 superspaces, as well as the component formulation in Minkowski space, directly from this unfolded system. We also comment on a putative off-shell extension of the on-shell system we constructed, and show how the harmonic contribution is reflected in the universal unfolded fiber.

### [53] [$S^3$ partition functions and Equivariant CY$_4 $/ CY$_3$ correspondence from Quantum curves](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19159)
*Kiril Hristov,Naotaka Kubo,Yi Pang*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper studies the large-N expansion of the S^3 partition function for M2-brane theories using Fermi gas and quantum curve methods, confirms an Airy-function representation matching topological string predictions for several toric Calabi–Yau geometries, and proposes a novel equivariant correspondence between CY4 and C×CY3 spaces linked to quantum curve equivalences—shedding light on the geometric origin of the TS/ST correspondence and holography.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand the geometric origin of the topological string/spectral theory (TS/ST) correspondence and its role in holography, particularly by testing and extending a recent proposal linking equivariant constant maps in topological string theory to exact partition functions of 3d N=2 and N=6 supersymmetric gauge theories.

Method: Applies the Fermi gas formalism and quantum curve techniques to compute the perturbative large-N expansion of the round S^3 partition function for flavored SYM, ABJM, and general 3d theories with (p,q) 5-brane web duals; derives Airy-function asymptotics and compares against equivariant topological string predictions; formulates a new equivariant CY4 ↔ C×CY3 correspondence via constrained quantum curve equivalences.

Result: Exact agreement is found between the Airy-function representation of the partition function and topological string predictions for C×C (conifold), C(Q^{1,1,1}), and C×SPP; a novel equivariant correspondence between fourfold and product threefold toric Calabi–Yau geometries is proposed, rooted in quantum curve relations.

Conclusion: The results affirm the TS/ST correspondence in equivariant settings and suggest its deeper geometric foundation lies in quantum curve equivalences; the proposed CY4 ↔ C×CY3 correspondence extends TS/ST to higher-dimensional Calabi–Yau geometries and provides new structural insight into AdS4/CFT3 holography.

Abstract: We study the perturbative large-$N$ expansion of the round three-sphere partition function in a class of M2-brane theories, including flavored SYM and ABJM theories as well as more general 3d theories admitting dual $(p,q)$ 5-brane web descriptions. Using the Fermi gas formalism and quantum curve techniques, we derive the Airy-function representation of the partition function and find exact agreement with predictions based on equivariant constant maps in topological string theory proposed in [1]. In particular, we provide affirmative tests of this proposal for the toric geometries $\mathbb{C} \times \mathcal{C}$ (the conifold), the cone over the Sasakian space $Q^{1,1,1}$, and $\mathbb{C} \times \mathrm{SPP}$ (the suspended pinch point). Motivated by a recent conjecture in [2], we further propose a novel equivariant correspondence between distinct toric Calabi-Yau manifolds of the form $\mathrm{CY}_4 \leftrightarrow \mathbb{C} \times\mathrm{CY}_3$, arising from relations between the corresponding quantum curves under specific constraints. This correspondence suggests an equivariant extension and points toward a geometric origin of the topological string/spectral theory (TS/ST) correspondence, while offering new insight into the structure of the holography duality.

### [54] [ADAMOS: Axion Daily Modulation Searches for Dark Matter at 20 GHz](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18006)
*Marios Maroudas,Toma-Stefan Cezar,Antonios Gardikiotis,Dieter Horns*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: ADAMOS is a novel axion haloscope experiment at 20 GHz using a thin-shell cavity in a 14 T magnet, featuring continuous in situ RF calibration to search simultaneously for cold DM axions, relativistic axions from AQN annihilations (with daily modulation), and transient streaming DM signals.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe an unexplored high-frequency (20 GHz) region of the axion dark matter parameter space, leveraging improved experimental robustness and calibration to overcome limitations of prior axion searches.

Method: Design and construction of a fixed-frequency, thin-shell superconducting cavity resonator operating at 20 GHz inside a 14 T magnet; integration with a highly sensitive, continuously calibrated RF detection chain to suppress temperature-dependent gain drifts.

Result: Enables simultaneous, high-sensitivity searches for three distinct axion-like DM signatures—cold DM axions, daily-modulated relativistic axions from axion quark nugget annihilations, and transient streaming DM enhancements—in a previously inaccessible frequency band.

Conclusion: ADAMOS establishes a new, calibrated, and versatile platform for axion DM detection, significantly expanding discovery potential in the high-mass axion regime and opening novel channels into the dark sector.

Abstract: The ADAMOS (Axion Daily Modulation Searches) project aims to explore the nature of dark matter (DM) through a novel axion haloscope experiment. We propose to construct a fixed-frequency cavity resonator operating at 20 GHz at the University of Hamburg, using an innovative "thin-shell" design that preserves a large detection volume at high frequencies. The experiment will be installed in an existing 14 T superconducting magnet and connected to a highly sensitive RF chain with continuous in situ calibration to eliminate temperature-dependent gain drifts, constituting an essential improvement based on lessons learned from previous attempts. ADAMOS will conduct simultaneous searches for three classes of axion signals: (1) conventional cold DM axions, (2) relativistic axions from axion quark nugget annihilations exhibiting daily modulations, and (3) transient enhancements from streaming DM. By targeting this unexplored frequency regime with a robust, calibrated, and versatile setup, ADAMOS will open new discovery channels in a previously unexplored region of the dark sector.

### [55] [A search for lepton-flavour violating $τ\to 3μ$ decays with the ATLAS detector](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18099)
*ATLAS Collaboration*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: This paper reports a search for charged lepton flavour violation in τ→3μ decays using 137 fb⁻¹ of 13 TeV pp collision data from ATLAS (2016–2018), focusing on the W→τν production channel; no significant signal is observed, leading to an upper limit of B(τ→3μ) < 8.7×10⁻⁸ at 90% CL.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To test the Standard Model's prediction of lepton flavour conservation by probing extremely rare or forbidden decays — specifically, charged lepton flavour violation (cLFV) in τ→3μ — which would signal new physics beyond the Standard Model.

Method: Analysis of ATLAS data using two- and three-muon triggers; selection of events from W→τν with subsequent τ→3μ decay; multivariate analysis for background suppression; unbinned maximum-likelihood fit to the three-muon invariant mass spectrum to extract limits.

Result: No significant excess over the expected background is observed; the data are consistent with the background-only hypothesis; the 90% CL upper limit on the branching ratio is B(τ→3μ) < 8.7×10⁻⁸ (observed) and 7.5×10⁻⁸ (expected).

Conclusion: The result sets the most stringent limit to date on τ→3μ decay, constraining models of new physics that induce cLFV, such as supersymmetry, leptoquarks, or extended Higgs sectors.

Abstract: A search for charged lepton flavour violation in $τ\to 3μ$ decays is performed in $pp$ collisions at a centre-of-mass energy of 13 TeV using ATLAS data collected between 2016 and 2018, corresponding to an integrated luminosity of 137 $\text{fb}^{-1}$. The search focuses on the electroweak $W \to τν$ production channel. Data are collected using two-muon and three-muon triggers and a multivariate analysis is used to separate the signal from the background. An unbinned likelihood fit is then performed to the resulting three-muon invariant mass spectrum and the data are found to be compatible with the background-only hypothesis. The observed (expected) limit on the branching ratio $B(τ\to3μ)$ is found to be $8.7\times 10^{-8}$ ($7.5\times 10^{-8}$) at $90\%$ CL.

</details>


### [56] [Reconstruction of overlapping electromagnetic showers in calorimeters using Transformers](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18172)
*Yuliia Maidannyk,Fabrice Couderc,Julie Malclès,Mehmet Özgür Sahin*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: This paper introduces ClusTEX, a graph transformer-based deep learning model for electromagnetic energy clustering in calorimeters, featuring geometry-aware positional encoding; it outperforms standard and two-step DL methods—especially under overlapping showers, boosted topologies, pileup, and detector failures—by jointly optimizing seed selection and reconstruction in a single inference pass.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Accurate clustering of electromagnetic energy deposits is critical for photon/electron reconstruction in hadron colliders, but is challenged by overlapping showers from boosted topologies and pileup, leading to ambiguous energy assignment.

Method: Proposes two deep learning approaches: (1) a two-step strategy using seed windows followed by distance-weighted message passing or attention-based interaction, and (2) ClusTEX—a single-stage graph transformer with novel positional encoding that decouples local graph coordinates from global η–φ detector coordinates. Trained on GEANT4 simulations of toy and ECAL-inspired calorimeter geometries with explicit η–φ dependence.

Result: In the toy calorimeter, attention-based models improve overlapping-shower reconstruction vs. standard algorithm and distance-driven message passing, maintain isolated-photon performance, reduce splitting, and preserve di-photon mass resolution for boosted π⁰→γγ. In the ECAL-inspired setup, ClusTEX achieves best overall performance: superior energy resolution, lower splitting rate, and robustness to localized detector failures—including partial energy recovery in dead channels.

Conclusion: ClusTEX establishes a new state-of-the-art for calorimeter clustering by unifying candidate selection and reconstruction in one geometry-aware, attention-driven inference stage, demonstrating significant gains in accuracy, robustness, and efficiency under realistic collider conditions.

Abstract: Accurate clustering of electromagnetic energy deposits is essential for reconstructing photons and electrons in modern hadron collider experiments, where boosted topologies and pileup cause overlapping showers and ambiguous energy assignment. We present deep learning-based clustering approaches that reconstruct particle energy and position directly from calorimeter readout. The study includes a two-step strategy in which candidate seed windows are identified and then jointly processed via distance-weighted message passing or attention mechanism and a single-step graph transformer, ClusTEX, which performs candidate selection and reconstruction in one inference stage. ClusTEX uses a novel positional encoding scheme that separates local coordinates within the graph from global detector coordinates, enabling efficient, geometry-aware inference. Models are trained on GEANT4 simulations of a simplified (toy) and an ECAL-inspired topology with an explicit $η-φ$ dependence. Performance is evaluated using efficiency, energy and position resolutions and splitting rate - reconstruction of two objects for a single photon. In the toy calorimeter, attention-based interactions improve the reconstruction of overlapping showers relative to both the standard algorithm and distance-driven message passing, while maintaining performance on isolated photons and reducing splitting without multi-pass inference. For boosted $π^0\toγγ$, the attention-based model retains di-photon mass reconstruction capability, where the standard algorithm becomes inefficient. In the ECAL-inspired topology, ClusTEX provides the best overall performance, yielding improved energy resolution and reduced splitting compared to two-step approaches and the standard algorithm. It also remains robust under localized detector failures, showing improved stability and partial recovery of energy in non-responsive channels.

</details>

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: First observation of D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η decay; large branching fraction for a_0(980)^+ f_0(500) intermediate state; dominant contribution from D_s^+ → a_1(1260)^+η → ρ(770)^+π^0 η; isospin symmetry confirmed; precise constraint on unobserved η′-related backgrounds.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe the internal structure of light scalar mesons (e.g., a_0(980), f_0(500)) and test QCD-inspired models via rare charm-strange meson decays, particularly those involving multiple neutral pseudoscalars and scalars.

Method: Analysis of 7.33 fb⁻¹ e⁺e⁻ collision data collected by BESIII at √s = 4.128–4.226 GeV; full reconstruction of D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η using kinematic fits, amplitude analysis, and intermediate resonance modeling (a_0(980), f_0(500), a_1(1260), ρ(770)); background suppression via particle ID and mass constraints.

Result: First observation of D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η with >10σ significance; B(D_s^+ → a_0(980)^+ f_0(500)) = (0.98 ± 0.16 ± 0.22)%; dominant B(D_s^+ → a_1(1260)^+η → ρ(770)^+π^0 η) = (1.77 ± 0.21 ± 0.12)%; isospin symmetry validated in a_1^+ decays; B(D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η|non-η′) = (2.97 ± 0.23 ± 0.14)×10⁻³; residual undetected D_s^+ → ηX < 0.1% (consistent with zero).

Conclusion: The unexpectedly large a_0(980)^+ f_0(500) rate challenges conventional quark-model expectations and supports tetraquark or molecular interpretations for light scalars; the dominance of a_1(1260)^+η channel confirms axial-vector mediation in D_s^+ decays; results provide benchmark inputs for lattice QCD and effective field theories of charm hadron decays.

Abstract: We report the first observation of the decay $D_s^+ \to π^+π^0π^0η$ in a data set corresponding to an integrated luminosity of 7.33 fb$^{-1}$, collected in $e^+e^-$ collisions by the BESIII detector at center-of-mass energies between 4.128 and 4.226 GeV. An unexpectedly large branching fraction $\mathcal{B}( D_s^+ \to a_0(980)^+ f_0(500), a_0(980)^+ \to π^+η, f_0(500)\to π^0π^0) = (0.98 \pm 0.16_{\rm{stat.}} \pm 0.22_{\rm{syst.}})\%$ is measured with a significance exceeding $10σ$, offering new constraints on the internal structure of light scalar mesons. The dominant intermediate process is $D_s^+ \to a_1(1260)^+η, a_1(1260)^+\to ρ(770)^+π^0$ with a branching fraction of $(1.77 \pm 0.21_{\rm stat.} \pm 0.12_{\rm syst.})\%$. The isospin symmetry has been validated to the decays of $a_1(1260)^+\to ρ(770)^0π^+$ and $a_1(1260)^+\to ρ(770)^+π^0$. Moreover, the measured $\mathcal{B}(D_s^+\to π^+π^0π^0η|_{\rm{non}-η^\prime})=(2.97 \pm 0.23_{\rm stat.} \pm 0.14_{\rm sys.})$ reduces the undetected $D_s^+ \to ηX$ decay branching fractions to (0.1 $\pm$ 3.1)\%.

### [58] [Combined effective field theory interpretation of measurements sensitive to quartic gauge boson couplings in $pp$ collisions at $\sqrt{s}=13$ TeV with the ATLAS detector](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18630)
*ATLAS Collaboration*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: This paper presents a combined ATLAS analysis of anomalous quartic electroweak gauge boson couplings using 13 TeV pp collision data, constraining dimension-8 operators in the Éboli model via vector-boson scattering and tri-boson measurements within an EFT framework, with results reported as confidence intervals on Wilson coefficients—both with and without unitarity/positivity constraints.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe physics beyond the Standard Model by testing anomalous quartic gauge boson couplings (aQGCs), which are highly suppressed in the SM but enhanced in certain BSM scenarios; such couplings are accessible via high-energy vector-boson scattering and multi-boson production at the LHC.

Method: Combined statistical analysis of multiple ATLAS measurements—including VBS in multiple final states (e.g., same-sign WW, WZ, ZZ) and triboson (WWW, WWZ, etc.) processes—using an effective field theory (EFT) framework based on dimension-8 operators in the Éboli model; profiled likelihood fits to Wilson coefficients with and without theoretical constraints from tree-level unitarity and analyticity (positivity).

Result: Stringent 68% and 95% CL limits on one- and two-dimensional Wilson coefficient spaces (e.g., f_T0, f_T1, f_T2, f_T5, f_T6, f_M0–f_M7); inclusion of unitarity bounds significantly tightens allowed regions; simultaneous multi-parameter fits yield correlated constraints, revealing degeneracies and complementarity among channels.

Conclusion: No significant deviation from the Standard Model is observed; the combined analysis sets the most sensitive direct constraints to date on aQGCs parameterized by dimension-8 EFT operators, demonstrating the power of multi-channel combination and theoretical consistency requirements in EFT interpretations.

Abstract: A combination of measurements sensitive to anomalous quartic electroweak gauge boson couplings is presented using proton-proton collision data collected by the ATLAS detector at $\sqrt{s} = 13$ TeV at the LHC. Contributing analyses include measurements of vector-boson scattering in numerous final states as well as a tri-boson measurement. The combined measurement is used to constrain anomalous electroweak boson quartic self-couplings that result from dimension-8 operators in the Éboli model using an effective field theory. Results are presented as 68% and 95% confidence level intervals parameterised by one or two Wilson coefficients, both with and without unitarity constraints applied. Theoretical bounds from unitarity and positivity are overlaid where relevant. Confidence intervals obtained from simultaneous profiled fits to all Wilson coefficients are also presented.
