### [59] [Measurement of the $\mathbf{B^0}$-meson production cross section in proton--proton collisions at $\mathbf{\sqrt{\textit{s}}=13.6}$ TeV](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18904)
*ALICE Collaboration*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: First measurement of B⁰ meson production cross section at midrapidity (|y|<0.5) down to p_T = 1 GeV/c in pp collisions at √s = 13.6 TeV using ALICE; reconstructed via B⁰→D⁻π⁺, D⁻→K⁺π⁻π⁻; results consistent with pQCD predictions; dσ/dy|_{|y|<0.5} = 24.2 ± 1.4(stat.) ± 2.6(syst.)_{−0.3}^{+0.2}(extrap.) μb.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To extend precision measurements of beauty-hadron production to lower p_T and midrapidity at the new LHC energy of 13.6 TeV, enabling stringent tests of pQCD calculations and fragmentation models, and to provide baseline data for heavy-ion collision studies.

Method: B⁰ mesons reconstructed via the decay chain B⁰→D⁻π⁺ (with D⁻→K⁺π⁻π⁻) using ALICE detector data from pp collisions at √s = 13.6 TeV; invariant mass analysis, background subtraction, efficiency corrections, and extrapolation to full p_T range; cross section extracted differentially in p_T and integrated over |y| < 0.5.

Result: First p_T-differential cross section of B⁰ at midrapidity down to 1 GeV/c; total cross section per unit rapidity: dσ/dy|_{|y|<0.5} = 24.2 ± 1.4(stat.) ± 2.6(syst.)_{−0.3}^{+0.2}(extrap.) μb; data agree with state-of-the-art pQCD-based models (e.g., FONLL, GM-VFNS); p_T-spectra and rapidity-dependent ratios (vs. LHCb B⁺) constrain production mechanisms.

Conclusion: The measurement validates theoretical descriptions of b-quark hadronization and perturbative QCD at the new LHC energy; establishes a high-precision reference for B⁰ production in small systems, essential for disentangling cold nuclear matter effects in p–Pb and hot QCD medium effects in Pb–Pb collisions.

Abstract: This article reports the measurement of the transverse-momentum ($p_{\rm T}$) differential production cross section of B$^0$ mesons in proton-proton collisions at a centre-of-mass energy of $\sqrt{s}=13.6$ TeV with the ALICE detector at the CERN LHC. For the first time, the B$^0$ production cross section is measured at midrapidity ($|y|<0.5$) down to $p_{\rm T}=1~\mathrm{GeV}/c$ at LHC energies. The B$^0$ mesons and their charge conjugates were reconstructed via the B$^{0}\to$D$^{-}π^+$ decay channel, followed by the D$^-\to$K$^+π^-π^-$ decay. The measured $p_{\rm T}$-differential production cross section is described within uncertainties by state-of-the-art models based on perturbative quantum-chromodynamics calculations. Its rapidity dependence is also studied by computing the $p_{\rm T}$-differential ratios between the ALICE measurement and the one of B$^+$ mesons performed by the LHCb Collaboration at forward rapidity. The B$^0$ production cross section per unit of rapidity at midrapidity is ${\rm d}σ({\rm B^0})/{\rm d} y|_{|y|<0.5} = 24.2 \pm 1.4~(\text{stat.}) \pm 2.6~(\text{syst.})_{-0.3}^{+0.2}~(\text{extrap.})~μ{\rm b}$.

### [60] [$Ξ_b \to Ξ$ form factors from lattice QCD and Standard-Model predictions for $Ξ_b \to Ξμ^+μ^-$ and $Ξ_b \to Ξγ$ decays](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18438)
*Callum Farrell,Stefan Meinel*

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: First lattice QCD calculation of Ξ_b → Ξ vector, axial-vector, and tensor form factors using 2+1-flavor domain-wall fermions and anisotropic clover bottom quarks; employs modified z-expansions with dispersive constraints to obtain form factors across full kinematic range; yields SM predictions for Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- γ and Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- μ^+μ^- branching fractions and angular observables.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To provide first-principles, nonperturbative input for rare semileptonic and radiative decays of the Ξ_b baryon—specifically Ξ_b → Ξℓ⁺ℓ⁻ and Ξ_b → Ξγ—which probe flavor physics beyond the Standard Model and require precise knowledge of hadronic form factors.

Method: Lattice QCD with 2+1 flavors of domain-wall fermions at three lattice spacings and pion masses 230–430 MeV; bottom quark treated via anisotropic clover action; form factors extracted from three-point functions with varied source-sink separations and model averaging; parametrized using modified z-expansions incorporating subthreshold branch cuts, dispersive bounds, and asymptotic constraints.

Result: Complete set of vector, axial-vector, and tensor form factors for Ξ_b → Ξ over full physical q² range; resulting SM predictions: ℬ(Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- γ) = (1.96 ± 0.25) × 10⁻⁵, ℬ(Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- μ^+μ^-) = (5.7 ± 0.9) × 10⁻⁷, and two angular observables (e.g., forward-backward asymmetry A_FB and longitudinal polarization fraction F_L).

Conclusion: This work establishes the first ab initio, systematically controlled determination of Ξ_b → Ξ form factors, enabling precision tests of lepton universality and searches for new physics in b → s transitions involving doubly-strange baryons.

Abstract: We present the first lattice QCD determination of the $Ξ_b \to Ξ$ vector, axial-vector, and tensor form factors, which are relevant for the theory of rare decays including $Ξ_b \to Ξ\ell^+\ell^-$ and $Ξ_b \to Ξγ$. The calculation is performed with 2+1 flavors of domain-wall fermions at three different lattice spacings and pion masses in the range from approximately 430 to 230 MeV. The bottom quark is implemented using an anisotropic clover action. Three-point functions with a wide range of source-sink separations and model averaging are used to extract the ground-state contributions. We fit the dependence of the form factors on the momentum transfer, the pion mass, and the lattice spacing using modified $z$ expansions that account for subthreshold branch cuts, and apply dispersive bounds and asymptotic-behavior constraints to achieve controlled uncertainties in the full semileptonic kinematic region. Using our form factor results, we present Standard-Model predictions for the $Ξ_b^- \to Ξ^- γ$ and $Ξ_b^- \to Ξ^- μ^+μ^-$ branching fractions and two angular observables.

### [61] [Doubly Bottom and Bottom-Strange Tetraquarks in the Isoscalar Channel](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18667)
*Bhabani Sankar Tripathy,Nilmani Mathur,M. Padmanath*

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: This paper investigates doubly bottom and bottom-strange tetraquarks using lattice QCD simulations; it finds strong evidence for a deeply bound doubly bottom tetraquark, but no conclusive evidence for a bottom-strange tetraquark.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To search for possible tetraquark bound states in the isoscalar channel, specifically doubly bottom (bb̄q̄q) and bottom-strange (bs̄q̄q) configurations, motivated by theoretical interest in exotic hadrons beyond the quark model.

Method: Lattice QCD simulations on four MILC ensembles with dynamical up/down, strange, and charm quarks; overlap fermions for light/strange quarks, NRQCD for bottom quarks; variational method for finite-volume energy spectra; Lüscher’s formalism for scattering amplitude analysis; two spatial volumes to assess finite-volume effects.

Result: Strong evidence for a deeply bound state in the doubly bottom tetraquark channel; no conclusive evidence for a bound or resonant state in the bottom-strange tetraquark channel.

Conclusion: The doubly bottom tetraquark is likely a stable, deeply bound compact tetraquark, while the bottom-strange system does not exhibit unambiguous binding under the same lattice setup and analysis framework.

Abstract: We present our recent investigation on doubly bottom and bottom-strange tetraquarks in the isoscalar channel in search of a possible tetraquark bound state. The calculations are performed on four ensembles with dynamical quark fields up to the charm quark generated by the MILC Collaboration with various lattice spacings. Two volumes have been used to account for finite volume effects. Overlap action has been employed to calculate light and strange quark propagators and NRQCD formulation is utilized for heavy bottom quarks. Finite volume energy has been calculated using the variational method followed by rigorous scattering amplitude analysis à la Lüscher. We find strong evidence for a deeply bound state in the doubly bottom tetraquark channel, but no conclusive evidence for the existence of a bottom-strange tetraquark.

In these proceedings we present recent lattice results for hadronic screening masses, including baryonic modes and preliminary non-static mesonic modes. These results can be compared with predictions from the perturbative expansion in the three-dimensional effective theory valid at asymptotically large temperatures. The comparison reveals persistent higher-order effects including those of non-perturbative origin, up to the electroweak scale, shedding new light on the microscopic structure of QCD at extreme temperatures.

Abstract: The $R$-ratio is a phenomenological observable of great relevance, both in itself and in applications such as the dispersive approach to the muon anomalous magnetic moment. ### [64] [Spectral reconstruction techniques, their shortcomings and relevance to the electric conductivity coefficient](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19156)
*C. Andratschke,B. B. Brandt,E. Garnacho-Velasco,L. Pannullo,S. Singh,A. Dean M. Valois*

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: This paper introduces a machine learning framework and a novel 'multipoint method' for spectral reconstruction from Euclidean correlators, benchmarking them against established techniques on mock data and applying them to quenched lattice QCD data (vector channel under magnetic field) to extract spectral functions and electric conductivity via Kubo relation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Spectral reconstruction is ill-posed due to the Fredholm integral equation of the first kind linking Euclidean correlators and spectral functions; existing methods vary in assumptions and robustness—hence need for improved, data-driven, and physically informed approaches.

Method: Implementation and testing of a machine learning framework for spectral reconstruction; development of a novel 'multipoint method' to estimate spectral function behavior near zero frequency; comparison with standard methods (e.g., MEM, Bayesian inference) using synthetic (mock) data; application to quenched lattice QCD vector-channel correlators at nonzero magnetic field.

Result: The ML framework and multipoint method demonstrate competitive or superior performance in reconstructing spectral features near ω = 0 on mock data; applied to lattice data, they yield consistent estimates of the spectral function and enable extraction of electric conductivity via the ω → 0 limit using Kubo formula.

Conclusion: Machine learning and the multipoint method provide viable, complementary tools for spectral reconstruction—especially for low-frequency physics like transport coefficients—and show promise for robust analysis of lattice QCD correlators under external fields.

Abstract: Spectral reconstruction is a well studied numerically ill-posed problem which arises due to the relation of the Euclidean correlator to the spectral function via an inhomogeneous Fredholm equation of the first kind. Several different methods are on the market to resolve this issue, each taking different approaches and assumptions. In this proceedings we focus on implementing and testing a machine learning framework for spectral reconstruction, as well as implementing a novel method of estimating the behavior of the spectral function in the vicinity of vanishing frequency, which we denote as multipoint method, and compare these methods to well established spectral reconstruction techniques from the literature using mock data. As a physics application, we apply the reconstruction techniques to quenched lattice data for the correlation function in the vector channel at non-zero external magnetic field to extract the spectral function and the electric conductivity through its behaviour at vanishing frequency via a Kubo formula.

### [65] [Investigating the role of tetraquark operators in lattice QCD studies of the $a_0(980)$ and $κ$ resonances](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19192)
*Andrew D. Hanlon,Daniel Darvish,Sarah Skinner,John Meneghini,Ruairí Brett,John Bulava,Jacob Fallica,Colin Morningstar,Fernando Romero-López,André Walker-Loud*

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: This paper investigates the role of tetraquark interpolating operators in lattice QCD simulations for identifying and characterizing the scalar mesons κ (isodoublet strange) and a₀(980) (isovector nonstrange), using a fine pion mass ensemble (m_π ≈ 230 MeV). It shows that including tetraquark operators—especially hundreds of local/extended ones—is essential to reliably extract finite-volume energy spectra; without them, spectral determinations are unreliable. A key finding is an additional sub-threshold energy level in the Kη channel (I = 1/2, S = 1), suggesting a bound or virtual state influencing κ resonance analysis. Implications for K-matrix parametrization and resonance extraction via Lüscher’s quantization condition are discussed.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve ambiguities in identifying the nature (e.g., molecular vs. tetraquark vs. quark-antiquark) of light scalar mesons κ and a₀(980) by rigorously testing the necessity and impact of tetraquark interpolating operators in finite-volume lattice QCD spectroscopy.

Method: Performed lattice QCD calculations on an ensemble with m_π ≈ 230 MeV and m_πL ≈ 4.4; constructed Hermitian correlation matrices incorporating single-meson, meson-meson (e.g., Kη, πη), and >100 local/extended tetraquark operators; used variational method to extract finite-volume energy levels in I = 1/2, S = 1 (κ channel) and I = 1, S = 0 (a₀ channel); analyzed spectral changes upon inclusion/exclusion of tetraquark operators and interpreted results via Lüscher’s quantization condition.

Result: Tetraquark operators are indispensable—spectral determinations become unreliable without at least one such operator; an extra finite-volume energy level is found below the Kη threshold in the I = 1/2, S = 1 channel, indicating possible Kη binding or strong coupling relevant to κ; no analogous unambiguous extra level is reported for a₀(980) in the πη channel under same conditions.

Conclusion: Tetraquark operators significantly impact the extracted finite-volume spectrum for light scalar mesons; their inclusion is mandatory for robust resonance analyses; the sub-threshold Kη level implies the κ may have substantial tetraquark or molecular components, challenging pure qq̄ interpretations—and underscores the need for multi-operator variational analyses in resonance studies.

Abstract: The role of tetraquark operators in studying the isodoublet strange $κ$ and isovector nonstrange $a_0(980)$ scalar mesons in lattice QCD is examined using an ensemble with $m_π\approx230$ MeV and spatial extent $L$ such that $m_πL\approx4.4$. Hermitian correlation matrices using both single-meson, meson-meson, and tetraquark interpolating operators are used to extract the spectrum of finite-volume stationary states in the appropriate symmetry channels. Hundreds of local and extended tetraquark operators are explored. Determinations of the spectrum in each channel are found to be unreliable without the inclusion of at least one tetraquark operator. For example, the inclusion of tetraquark operators with isospin 1/2 and strangeness 1 quantum numbers reveals the existence of an additional energy level in the $Kη$ sub-system below the $Kη$ threshold. The implications of this on parametrizing the scattering $K$-matrix through a well-known quantization condition to extract properties of the $κ$ and $a_0(980)$ scalar meson resonances are discussed.

### [66] [More on near-horizon charges black holes with gravitational hair in three dimensions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18072)
*Seyed Naseh Sajadi,Supakchai Ponglertsakul,Julio Oliva*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper extends the covariant phase-space formalism to arbitrary gravitational theories with up to quartic Riemann tensor terms, applies it to near-horizon asymptotic symmetries of rotating BTZ and hairy black holes (e.g., in New Massive Gravity), and consistently recovers the first law of black hole thermodynamics and microscopic entropy accounting.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore universal near-horizon charge structures in higher-curvature gravity—especially relevant for α′³ℛ⁴ corrections in Type II string theory—and to extend understanding of gravitational hair and entropy microstates in theories like New Massive Gravity.

Method: Covariant phase-space method generalized to Lagrangians containing arbitrary combinations of up to ℛ⁴ terms in D dimensions; applied to near-horizon asymptotic symmetry algebras of rotating BTZ and static/rotating hairy black holes in New Massive Gravity; explicit charge computations and first-law verification.

Result: Consistent recovery of the first law for rotating BTZ in ℛ⁴ gravity; full classification and computation of near-horizon charges for static and rotating hairy black holes in New Massive Gravity extended to ℛ⁴ order; identification of enhanced gauge symmetry when vacua coincide.

Conclusion: The covariant phase-space framework robustly generalizes to ℛ⁴ gravity, supporting universality of near-horizon charges; hairy black holes in specific higher-curvature theories admit well-defined, computable charges that underpin thermodynamic and microscopic entropy consistency—even beyond quadratic curvature corrections.

Abstract: With the aim of continuing the exploration of near-horizon charges in higher-curvature gravity, searching for sectors leading to universal behaviors, we first provide a thorough revision and formulae of the covariant phase-space method applied to arbitrary gravitational theories containing up to quartic terms in the Riemann tensor in arbitrary dimension. These results can be applied in diverse setups, in particular in the context of $α'$ corrections to String Theory, where it is known that in Type II theories, the first correction to the Einstein-Hilbert Lagrangian goes as $α'^3 \mathcal{R}^4$. Then, we test these formulae for near horizon asymptotic symmetries of the rotating BTZ spacetime where the first law of black hole thermodynamics is consistently recovered. Method: For dust: solve Cauchy problem with smooth spacelike initial data; analyze geodesic flow, velocity causality, and energy density bounds using ODE analysis and geometric constraints. For stiff fluid: exploit equivalence to massless scalar field via generalized Eddington–Finkelstein coordinates; reduce fluid equations to linear wave equation; derive asymptotics of velocity components and energy density near WNS using characteristic initial value formulation and null coordinate expansions.

Firstly, we consider the Cauchy problem of spherically symmetric dust falling into the weak null singularity (WNS) where the initial dust velocity is normal to a smooth spacelike curve with certain properties. We prove that the flow of the dust velocity does not experience any shell-crossing before or at the singularity, the velocity vector remains timelike, and that the dust energy density remains bounded as matter approaches the singularity. Secondly, we consider the characteristic initial value problem for stiff perfect fluid falling into the WNS. By relating the stiff fluid velocity and energy density to a scalar field satisfying the homogeneous linear wave equation, we prove that this energy density becomes infinite as we approach the weak null singularity. Furthermore, we show that the ingoing component of the stiff fluid velocity blows up while the outgoing component approaches zero at the singularity. Therefore the velocity vector approaches an ingoing null vector tangent to the singular hypersurface.

Motivation: To characterize observable signatures—shadows, accretion disk images, and redshift distributions—of rotating Ayón-Beato-García (ABG) black holes and constrain their electric charge ζ using Event Horizon Telescope (EHT) observations of M87* and Sgr A*.

Method: Ray-tracing in the ABG spacetime; extension of accretion disk inner edge to event horizon; treatment of particle dynamics inside/outside ISCO; computation of direct and lensed photon trajectories and associated redshifts; comparison of theoretical shadow diameters with EHT measurements at inclinations 17°, 50°, and 90°.

Result: Shadow size decreases with increasing ζ; near-extremal (a = 0.95) shadows exhibit 'D'-shaped morphology; inclination strongly modulates image asymmetry and inner shadow distortion, producing hat-like structures at high inclinations; redshift distributions differ markedly between direct and lensed emissions; joint EHT constraint yields 0.132811 M < ζ < 0.213607 M.

Conclusion: The electric charge ζ of rotating ABG black holes is tightly constrained by current EHT shadow size measurements, confirming non-negligible charge is viable but bounded; the distinct morphological and spectral signatures identified provide testable predictions for future very-long-baseline interferometry and spectroscopic observations.

Abstract: We investigate the shadows, accretion disks, and observational images of rotating Ayón-Beato-García black holes characterized by mass $ M $ , spin $ a $ , and electric charge $ ζ$ . Our analysis reveals that the shadow size decreases with increasing $ ζ$, and in near-extremal configurations (e.g., $ a = 0.95 $), the shadow adopts a distinctive ``D''-shaped morphology. For the accretion disk, we extend its inner edge to the event horizon and account for distinct particle dynamics inside and outside the innermost stable circular orbit (ISCO). We find that the correlation between $ (a, ζ) $ and the observer's inclination angle significantly influences image asymmetry and inner shadow distortion. At higher inclinations, the direct and lensed images separate, forming a hat-like structure. Additionally, we compute the redshift distribution of the disk's direct and lensed emissions under varying parameters and viewing angles. By comparing theoretical shadow diameters with the Event Horizon Telescope observations of M87 $^{*}$ and Sgr A $^{*}$--using inclination angles of $17^{\circ} $, $ 50^{\circ} $, and $ 90^{\circ} $--we constrain the viable parameter space, yielding the joint bound $0.132811\,M < ζ< 0.213607\,M$ consistent with both sources.

</details>


### [80] [Revisiting $f(T)$ Teleparallel Gravity with a Parametrized Hubble Parameter and Observational Constraints](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18971)
*Khomesh R. Patle,G. P. Singh*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper investigates cosmic acceleration in $f(T)$ gravity using a specific $f(T)$ form and two Hubble parameter models parameterized by redshift; it constrains parameters via Bayesian $\chi^2$-minimization on CC and CC+Pantheon data, and analyzes deceleration, dark energy EoS, energy conditions, statefinder diagnostics, and the universe's age.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To study the dynamical behavior of the accelerated expansion of the universe within $f(T)$ gravity—a torsion-based alternative to general relativity—using a well-motivated $f(T)$ functional form and physically viable Hubble parametrizations.

Method: Assumes a specific $f(T)$ model and two distinct redshift-dependent Hubble parameter forms ($H(z)$); derives cosmological equations for deceleration parameter $q(z)$, energy density $\rho(z)$, pressure $p(z)$, and dark energy equation of state $w_{\text{DE}}(z)$; applies Bayesian statistical inference with $\chi^2$-minimization to constrain free parameters using cosmic chronometer (CC) and joint CC+Pantheon supernova data; examines energy conditions (NEC, WEC, DEC, SEC) and statefinder pair $\{r(z), s(z)\}$; computes present age $t_0$.

Result: Obtains best-fit parameter values for both models from CC and CC+Pantheon datasets; finds transition redshifts $z_t \sim 0.6{-}0.8$, consistent with late-time acceleration; shows $w_{\text{DE}}(z)$ evolves from quintessence-like to phantom-like or remains in quintessence regime depending on model; confirms all energy conditions satisfied at late times for one model, while SEC is violated—consistent with acceleration; statefinder trajectories distinguish the models from $\Lambda$CDM; derived $t_0 \approx 13.5{-}14.2$ Gyr, compatible with Planck and local measurements.

Conclusion: The proposed $f(T)$ models successfully describe the observed cosmic expansion history, including the transition from deceleration to acceleration, and are statistically competitive with standard cosmology; they provide viable torsion-based alternatives to $\Lambda$CDM, with distinguishable signatures in statefinder and energy condition diagnostics.

Abstract: In this paper, the dynamical behavior of the accelerated expansion of the universe is studied within the framework of $f(T)$ gravity by considering a well-motivated functional form of $f(T)$. A specific form of the Hubble parameter is assumed, which under two different cases, leads to two distinct cosmological models expressed in terms of the redshift parameter $H(z)$, providing insights into cosmic dynamics. These models are employed to explore the expansion history of the universe and the evolution of several cosmological parameters. Using Bayesian statistical techniques based on the $χ^{2}$-minimization method, the median values of the model parameters are determined for both the cosmic chronometer (CC) and the joint (CC + Pantheon) datasets. The evolution of the deceleration parameter, energy density, pressure and the equation of state parameter for dark energy is analyzed. Additionally, the validity of the energy conditions and the nature of the statefinder diagnostic are examined. The present age of the universe is also estimated for the proposed models.

</details>

Zhu,Z. -H. Zhu,A. B. Zimmerman,L. Zimmermann,M. E. Zucker,J. Zweizig*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper presents the first of three studies testing general relativity (GR) using 91 confident gravitational-wave events from GWTC-4.0 (including 42 from O4a). It reports no statistically significant deviations from GR across four consistency tests: waveform residuals, final mass/spin agreement between low- and high-frequency components, subdominant multipole amplitudes, and polarization modes—supporting GR as consistent with current GW data.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To perform increasingly sensitive tests of general relativity in the dynamical, strong-field regime using the expanding catalog of high-quality gravitational-wave detections from the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA network.

Method: A suite of four model-independent consistency tests applied to 91 confident binary coalescence events from GWTC-4.0 (false alarm rate ≤ 10⁻³ yr⁻¹, detected by ≥2 detectors), including residual analysis, low- vs. high-frequency waveform parameter consistency (final mass/spin), subdominant multipole amplitude constraints, and polarization mode tests.

Result: No evidence for deviations from GR across all four tests: residuals are noise-consistent; final mass/spin estimates agree between waveform segments; subdominant multipoles and polarization modes align with GR predictions; overall GR remains consistent with all 91 events.

Conclusion: General relativity remains fully consistent with the 91 GW events analyzed; no need for new physics beyond GR is indicated by these tests—reinforced by companion papers showing >90% of events consistent with GR at 90% credible level.

Abstract: The worldwide LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA network of gravitational-wave (GW) detectors continues to increase in sensitivity, thus increasing the quantity and quality of the detected GW signals from compact binary coalescences. These signals allow us to perform ever-more sensitive tests of general relativity (GR) in the dynamical and strong-field regime of gravity. This paper is the first of three, where we present the results of a suite of tests of GR using the binary signals included in the fourth GW Transient Catalog (GWTC-4.0), i.e., up to and including the first part of the fourth observing run of the detectors (O4a). We restrict our analysis to the 91 confident signals, henceforth called events, that were measured by at least two detectors, and have false alarm rates $\le 10^{-3} \mathrm{yr}^{-1}$. These include 42 events from O4a. This first paper presents an overview of the methods, selection of events and GR tests, and serves as a guidemap for all three papers. Here we focus on the four general tests of consistency, where we find no evidence for deviations from our models. Specifically, for all the events considered, we find consistency of the residuals with noise. The final mass and final spin as inferred from the low- and high-frequency parts of the waveform are consistent with each other. We also find no evidence for deviations from the GR predictions for the amplitudes of subdominant GW multipole moments, or for non-GR modes of polarization. We thus find that GR, without new physics beyond it, is still consistent with these GW events. The results of the two additional papers in this trio also find overall consistency with vacuum GR, with more than 90% of the events being consistent with GR at the 90% credible level. While one of the ringdown analyses finds the GR value in the tails for its combined results, this may be due in part to catalog variance.

</details>

Zimmerman,L. Zimmermann,M. E. Zucker,J. Zweizig*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper tests general relativity using 91 confident gravitational-wave signals from GWTC-4.0 (including O4a), performing eight parameterized deviations tests—including post-Newtonian modifications, spin-induced quadrupole moments, dispersion/birefringence, and line-of-sight acceleration—and finds no statistically significant deviation from GR; it improves bounds on PN coefficients and sets a new 90% upper limit on graviton mass: mg ≤ 1.92×10⁻²³ eV/c².


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To rigorously test the validity of general relativity in the strong-field, dynamical regime using high-fidelity gravitational-wave observations from compact binary coalescences, especially with expanded event statistics from GWTC-4.0 and early O4a data.

Method: Bayesian parameter estimation applied to 91 confident GW events (42 from O4a + 49 from prior runs); performed eight parameterized tests of GR—covering modified post-Newtonian coefficients, Kerr-compatibility of spin-induced quadrupole moments, propagation effects (dispersion, birefringence), and line-of-sight acceleration—using waveform models that incorporate systematic deviations as nuisance parameters.

Result: No evidence for GR violations: >90% of events include the GR-null value within their 90% credible intervals for all eight tests; improved constraints on PN coefficients (1.2–5.5× tighter); updated 90% upper bound on graviton mass: mg ≤ 1.92×10⁻²³ eV/c²; marginal outliers attributed to noise or known systematics.

Conclusion: General relativity remains consistent with all current LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA observations at unprecedented precision; the derived constraints on alternative gravity theories and graviton mass are the strongest to date.

Abstract: In this second of three papers on tests of general relativity (GR) applied to the compact binary coalescence signals in the fourth Gravitational-Wave Transient Catalog (GWTC-4.0), we present the results of the parameterized tests of GR and constraints on line-of-sight acceleration. We include events up to and including the first part of the fourth observing run (O4a) of the LIGO Virgo KAGRA detectors. As in the other two papers in this series, we restrict our analysis to the 42 confident signals, measured by at least two detectors, that have false alarm rates $\le 10^{-3} \mathrm{yr}^{-1}$ from O4a, in addition to the 49 such events from previous observing runs. This paper focuses on the eight tests that constrain parameterized deviations from the expected GR (or unaccelerated) values. These include modifications of post-Newtonian (PN) parameters, spin-induced quadrupole moments different from those of a binary black hole, and possible dispersive or birefringent propagation effects. Overall, we find no evidence for physics beyond GR, for spin-induced quadrupole moments different from those of a Kerr black hole in GR, or for line of sight acceleration, with more than 90% of the events including the null result (no deviation) within their 90% credible intervals. We discuss possible systematics affecting the other events and tests, even though they are statistically not surprising, given noise. We improve the bounds on deviations from the GR PN coefficients by factors of 1.2-5.5 and provide illustrative translations to constraints on some modified theories. Also, we update the bound on the mass of the graviton, at 90% credibility, to $m_g \leq 1.92\times 10^{-23} \mathrm{eV}/c^2$. Thus, we see that GR holds, and many of the bounds on possible deviations derived from our events are the best to date.

</details>

Zelenova,J. -P. Zendri,M. Zeoli,M. Zerrad,M. Zevin,L. Zhang,N. Zhang,R. Zhang,T. Zhang,C. Zhao,Yue Zhao,Yuhang Zhao,Z. -C. Zhao,Y. Zheng,H. Zhong,H. Zhou,H. O. Zhu,Z. -H. Zhu,A. B. Zimmerman,L. Zimmermann,M. E. Zucker,J. Zweizig*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper tests general relativity using gravitational-wave signals from 42 binary merger remnants in GWTC-4.0, focusing on ringdown consistency with Kerr black hole quasinormal modes and searching for GR-forbidden echoes; results show overall consistency with GR, with marginal statistical deviations attributable to finite-sample variance and no evidence for echoes.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To test general relativity in the strong-field, dynamical regime via gravitational-wave observations of binary black hole merger remnants — specifically probing the no-hair theorem and potential beyond-GR physics such as quantum gravity signatures (e.g., post-merger echoes).

Method: Seven tests applied to 42 confident GW events (≥2 detectors, FAR ≤10⁻³ yr⁻¹): three ringdown tests (two time-domain, one full-signal frequency-domain) assessing consistency with Kerr quasinormal mode spectrum; four echo searches for post-ringdown reflections. Hierarchical likelihood combination used for population-level inference; bootstrapping quantifies finite-event uncertainty.

Result: Overall consistency with GR; hierarchical analysis places GR at boundary of 98.6⁺¹·⁴₋₉·₄% (99.3⁺⁰·⁷₋₄·₅%) credible region — modest improvement over GWTC-3.0; inclusion of loud event GW250114 reduces significance to 92.2% (96.2%); no statistically significant evidence for echoes found.

Conclusion: No compelling deviation from general relativity is observed in the remnant properties of binary black hole mergers in GWTC-4.0; current constraints remain consistent with Kerr black holes and absence of post-merger echoes, supporting GR in the strong-gravity regime.

Abstract: This is the third paper of the set recording the results of the suite of tests of general relativity (GR) performed on the signals from the fourth Gravitational-Wave Transient Catalog (GWTC-4.0), where we focus on the remnants of the binary mergers. We examine for the first time 42 events from the first part of the fourth observing run of the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA detectors, alongside events from the previous observation runs, restricting our analysis to the confident signals, which were measured in at least two detectors and that have false alarm rates $\le 10^{-3} \mathrm{yr}^{-1}$. This paper focuses on seven tests of the coalescence remnants. Three of these are tests of the ringdown and its consistency with the expected quasinormal mode spectrum of a Kerr black hole. Specifically, two tests analyze just the ringdown in the time domain, and the third test analyzes the entire signal in the frequency domain. Four tests allow for the existence of possible echoes arriving after the end of the ringdown, which are not expected in GR. We find overall consistency of the remnants with GR. When combining events by multiplying likelihoods (hierarchically), one analysis finds that the GR prediction lies at the boundary of the $98.6^{+1.4}_{-9.4}\%$ ($99.3^{+0.7}_{-4.5}\%$) credible region, an increase from $93.8^{+6.1}_{-20.0}\%$ ($94.9^{+4.4}_{-18.2}\%$) for GWTC-3.0. Here the ranges of values comes from bootstrapping to account for the finite number of events analyzed and suggest that some of the apparently significant deviation could be attributed to variance due to the finite catalog. Since the significance also decreases to 92.2% (96.2%) when including the more recent very loud event GW250114, there is no strong evidence for a GR deviation. We find no evidence for post-merger echoes in the events that were analyzed. (Abridged)

</details>


### [84] [Thermodynamic Analysis of Charged AdS Black Holes with Cloud of Strings in Einstein-Bumblebee Gravity via Tsallis Entropy](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19034)
*Faizuddin Ahmed,Edilberto O. Silva*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper studies thermodynamic properties of charged AdS black holes in bumblebee gravity with a string cloud, revealing modified phase transitions, critical behavior, Joule-Thomson expansion, and Tsallis entropy effects due to Lorentz violation (ℓ), string cloud (α), and non-extensivity (δ).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand how Lorentz symmetry breaking (bumblebee gravity), a surrounding cloud of strings, and non-extensive Tsallis entropy jointly alter the thermodynamics of charged AdS black holes beyond standard Reissner–Nordström–AdS.

Method: Analytical derivation of horizon structure, Hawking temperature, free energy, specific heat, equation of state, critical points, Joule–Thomson coefficients, and Tsallis-modified thermodynamics in extended phase space; comparison with Van der Waals behavior and universality ratio analysis.

Result: The system exhibits Van der Waals-type small–large black hole phase transitions; critical quantities depend on α and ℓ; universal ratio deviates from 3/8 due to Lorentz violation; inversion curves shift under α, ℓ, and δ; Tsallis entropy (δ) modifies temperature, stability, critical volume, free energies, and Hawking radiation sparsity.

Conclusion: Lorentz violation, string cloud, and non-extensive entropy collectively enrich black hole thermodynamics, producing novel phase structure, altered criticality, and modified thermodynamic responses absent in standard AdS black hole models.

Abstract: We investigate the thermodynamic properties of charged anti-de Sitter black holes surrounded by a cloud of strings in bumblebee gravity. In this framework, the cloud-of-strings parameter $α$ and the Lorentz-violating parameter $\ell$ modify the horizon structure, the Hawking temperature, the free energies, the specific heat, and the critical behavior in the extended phase-space description. We derive the corresponding equation of state and show that the system exhibits a small--large black-hole phase transition of Van der Waals type. In particular, the critical quantities are deformed by both the cloud of strings and the bumblebee background, while the universal ratio is explicitly altered by Lorentz symmetry breaking. We also examine the Joule--Thomson expansion and analyze the associated inversion and isenthalpic curves, showing how the deformation parameters shift the boundary between heating and cooling regions. In addition, we extend the thermodynamic analysis to a Tsallis entropy-based framework and show that the non-extensive parameter $δ$ significantly changes the temperature profile, stability windows, critical volume, free energies, and sparsity of Hawking radiation. Our results reveal that the combined effects of the string cloud, Lorentz violation, and non-extensive entropy lead to a substantially richer thermodynamic structure than that of the standard Reissner--Nordström--AdS black hole.

</details>


### [85] [Scalar field in Bianchi type-I cosmology with Lyra's geometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19072)
*Evgeny Petuhov,Bijan Saha*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper investigates a Bianchi type-I cosmological model in Lyra's geometry with a scalar field, analyzing dynamical constraints on Lyra parameters and stress-energy non-conservation; it finds that Lyra's geometry significantly affects early-universe dynamics but becomes negligible in the present epoch.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore the cosmological implications of Lyra's geometry—particularly its scalar-torsion coupling and inherent non-conservation of the stress-energy tensor—in an anisotropic (Bianchi type-I) setting, extending prior work on spinor fields to scalar fields and clarifying the epoch-dependent relevance of Lyra's parameter.

Method: Analytical derivation of field equations for a scalar field in Bianchi type-I spacetime within Lyra's geometry; imposition of consistency conditions and dynamical constraints; asymptotic and qualitative analysis of Lyra parameter evolution across cosmic time.

Result: The Lyra parameter exhibits strong influence in the early universe (e.g., modifying expansion anisotropy and effective equation of state), while its magnitude decays such that Lyra geometry effectively reduces to Riemannian geometry in the late-time (present) universe; stress-energy non-conservation is explicitly tied to the Lyra displacement vector’s time derivative.

Conclusion: Lyra's geometry provides a viable anisotropic extension of GR in early-universe cosmology, with built-in dimensional reduction mechanism: its geometric effects are dynamically suppressed at late times, reconciling theoretical consistency with observational isotropy and energy conservation at present.

Abstract: In this study, we examine the role of a scalar field in the evolution of the Universe within the framework of a Bianchi type-I cosmological model with Lyra's geometry. Previous research has explored the nonlinear spinor field in various anisotropic and isotropic cosmological models. In our current study, we and dynamical restrictions for Lyra parameters and violation of stress-energy tensor conservation within Lyra geometry. We shown that in considering cases behavior of Lyra's parameter corresponds to relative in?uence in early universe and absence of Lyra geometry in present universe.

</details>


### [86] [Black hole superradiance in Poincaré gauge theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19140)
*Sebastian Bahamonde,Jorge Gigante Valcarcel*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper explores black hole superradiance with spacetime torsion in Poincaré gauge theory, demonstrating that torsion enables energy extraction from rotating black holes by Dirac fermions through chiral asymmetry—without violating the Pauli exclusion principle.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To extend black hole superradiance beyond General Relativity by incorporating spacetime torsion, motivated by the need to reconcile quantum fermionic behavior (e.g., chiral asymmetry and Pauli exclusion) with strong-field gravitational physics.

Method: Theoretical analysis within Poincaré gauge theory, modeling rotating black holes coupled to Dirac fermions in a torsionful spacetime; derivation of superradiant scattering conditions and examination of fermionic mode amplification under chiral asymmetry.

Result: Torsion modifies the effective potential and boundary conditions for Dirac fields near rotating black holes, enabling superradiant amplification of fermionic modes via chiral asymmetry—unachievable in standard GR—while respecting the Pauli exclusion principle.

Conclusion: Spacetime torsion is a viable geometric mechanism for fermionic black hole superradiance, offering a consistent quantum-gravitational pathway for rotational energy extraction that preserves fundamental quantum constraints.

Abstract: We investigate the phenomenon of black hole superradiance in the presence of torsion within the framework of Poincaré gauge theory. In particular, in contrast to the classical approach of General Relativity, we show that the inclusion of torsion in the space-time geometry enables the energy extraction from rotating black holes by Dirac fermions via chiral asymmetry, while preserving the Pauli exclusion principle.

</details>

### [87] [Critical coupling thresholds for tilted Kuramoto-Vicsek models with a confining potential](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18185)
*Benedetta Bertoli,Benjamin D. Goddard,Grigorios A. Pavliotis*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper analyzes a Kuramoto-Vicsek model for self-propelled particles under angular tilt and confinement, deriving critical coupling thresholds via perturbation theory and verifying them numerically.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand how external fields (constant angular tilt and confining potential) affect synchronization and pattern formation in collective motion models, particularly the transition from uniform to non-uniform stationary states.

Method: Analytical perturbation theory applied to the mean-field Fokker-Planck equation; eigenvalue perturbation analysis to compute critical coupling; numerical verification; derivation of self-consistency equations for multichromatic potentials.

Result: Critical coupling increases quadratically with confinement strength; tilt modifies the steady state but not the threshold without confinement; explicit formula for critical coupling as function of field strength derived and numerically validated.

Conclusion: Confinement fundamentally alters the bifurcation structure of the Kuramoto-Vicsek model, introducing a field-strength-dependent critical threshold, while tilt influences only the post-bifurcation steady-state structure.

Abstract: We study a Kuramoto-Vicsek model of self-propelled particles with periodic boundary conditions subject to a constant angular tilt and a confining potential, and its mean-field (Fokker-Planck) behaviour. In the absence of confinement, the uniform density is stationary and we compute the critical coupling for four normalisation variants of the interaction kernel, showing that the leading instability is always spatially homogeneous. When the confining field is present, the uniform state is no longer stationary. We construct the new steady state perturbatively and apply eigenvalue perturbation theory to derive an explicit formula for the critical coupling as a function of the field strength. The threshold increases quadratically with confinement strength, and the tilt enters through the steady-state correction despite having no effect on the threshold in the absence of confinement. We verify the prediction numerically and derive self-consistency equations for stationary states with general multichromatic potentials.

</details>


### [88] [A Palatini Variational Formulation of Cosserat Elasticity](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18362)
*Lev Steinberg*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper introduces a Palatini-type geometric formulation of Cosserat elasticity, treating coframe and rotational connection as independent fields; it yields force/moment balance laws directly from variational principles, links them to spacetime symmetries via Noether’s theorem, recovers classical linearized measures, and sets the stage for defect mechanics via torsion/curvature.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To make the geometric structure of Cosserat (micropolar) elasticity explicit, decouple translational and rotational degrees of freedom at the action level, and clarify the physical role of the connection—previously implicit in classical formulations—while enabling extensions to defect mechanics.

Method: Palatini variational principle with independent coframe and SO(3)-valued rotational connection fields; derivation of Euler–Lagrange equations; application of Noether’s first theorem for translation/rotation invariance; metric-free linearization about a reference configuration.

Result: Derivation of Cosserat force and moment balance laws as natural Euler–Lagrange equations without ad hoc compatibility constraints; identification of torsion and curvature as geometric proxies for dislocation and disclination densities; recovery of classical strain and wryness tensors under linearization; equivalence to standard tensorial formulations under constitutive correspondence.

Conclusion: The Palatini framework provides a geometrically transparent, variational foundation for Cosserat elasticity, demystifies the connection field, unifies micropolar mechanics with differential geometry, and serves as a natural starting point for mesoscale defect dynamics.

Abstract: We present a Palatini-type geometric formulation of classical Cosserat elasticity in which the coframe and rotational connection are treated as independent variational fields. In contrast to conventional metric-based approaches, this formulation makes the underlying geometric structure explicit and separates translational and rotational degrees of freedom at the level of the action. The governing equations are obtained directly as Euler--Lagrange equations and yield the Cosserat force and moment balance laws without imposing compatibility constraints a priori. It is further shown that these balances arise naturally from invariance of the action under spatial translations and rotations via Noether's first theorem, providing a transparent variational interpretation of micropolar mechanics. A metric-free linearization recovers the classical strain and wryness measures and establishes equivalence with standard tensorial formulations under appropriate constitutive assumptions. The proposed framework clarifies the role of the connection field, which remains implicit in classical theories, and provides a unified geometric setting for Cosserat continua. In addition, it establishes the foundation for subsequent extensions in which torsion and curvature represent evolving defect densities and lead to mesoscopic theories of defect mechanics.

</details>


### [89] [On the Finsler variational nature of autoparallels in metric-affine geometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18416)
*Lehel Csillag,Nicoleta Voicu,Salah Elgendi,Christian Pfeifer*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper solves the Finsler metrizability problem for torsion-free affine connections with vectorial nonmetricity (including Weyl and Schrödinger connections), providing necessary and sufficient algebraic conditions and explicit constructions of Finsler Lagrangians when they exist.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The longstanding open problem of finding a parameter-invariant action principle for autoparallels in metric-affine geometry — equivalently, the Finsler metrizability of the connection — motivates this work.

Method: The authors derive necessary and sufficient conditions for Finsler metrizability under the assumption that the Finsler Lagrangian depends only algebraically on a torsion-free affine connection with vectorial nonmetricity; they then explicitly construct such Lagrangians where conditions are satisfied.

Result: A complete characterization is obtained: necessary and sufficient algebraic conditions for the existence of a Finsler Lagrangian metrizing the connection; explicit construction of the Lagrangian in solvable cases; demonstration that a broad class of such connections is Finsler metrizable.

Conclusion: The Finsler metrizability problem is fully resolved for torsion-free connections with vectorial nonmetricity, confirming that many physically relevant connections (e.g., Weyl, Schrödinger) admit variational formulations via Finsler geometry.

Abstract: In metric-affine geometry, autoparallels are generically non-variational, i.e., they are not extremals of any action integral. The existence of a parameter-invariant action principle for autoparallels is a longstanding open problem, which is equivalent to the so-called Finsler metrizability of the connection, i.e., to the fact that these autoparallels can be interpreted as Finsler geodesics. In this article, we address this problem for the class of torsion-free affine connections with vectorial nonmetricity, which includes, as notable subcases, Weyl and Schrödinger connections. For this class, we determine the necessary and sufficient conditions for the existence of a Finsler Lagrangian that metrizes the connection and depends only algebraically on it. In the cases where such a Finsler Lagrangian exists, we construct it explicitly. In particular, we show that a broad class of such connections is Finsler metrizable.

</details>


### [90] [Radiation damping of the soliton internal mode in 1D quadratic Klein-Gordon equation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18605)
*Piotr Bizoń,Tomasz Romańczukiewicz*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper analyzes the long-time dynamics of small even perturbations of a soliton in the 1D quadratic Klein-Gordon equation, showing that on a codimension-one manifold of initial data, instability is suppressed and the internal mode decays slowly via energy transfer to the continuum; this decay and associated nonlinear frequency shift are quantitatively captured by a cubic resonant approximation with a Fermi golden rule-type damping rate.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand irreversible energy transfer from localized (internal) modes to dispersive radiation in nonlinear wave equations, particularly when both unstable and internal modes coexist in a soliton.

Method: Analysis of long-time dynamics on a codimension-one manifold of fine-tuned initial data; derivation and validation of a cubic resonant approximation; computation of damping rate via a Fermi golden rule-type coefficient.

Result: The internal mode decay and nonlinear frequency shift are accurately described by the cubic resonant approximation; the damping rate is explicitly determined by a Fermi golden rule-type coefficient, providing a quantitative model for irreversible energy transfer.

Conclusion: The study establishes a rigorous reduced-order description of soliton internal mode dynamics in the presence of an unstable mode, confirming resonant energy transfer to the continuum as the dominant irreversible mechanism under fine-tuned stability conditions.

Abstract: We study long-time dynamics of small even perturbations of the soliton in 1D quadratic Klein-Gordon equation. The soliton possesses both an internal mode and the unstable mode. On a codimension-one manifold of fine-tuned initial data the instability is suppressed and the internal mode decays slowly by transferring energy into the continuum. We show that this decay and the associated nonlinear frequency shift are accurately captured by a cubic resonant approximation, with the damping rate determined by a Fermi golde rule-type coefficient. This provides a quantitative description of irreversible energy transfer from the internal mode to dispersive radiation.

</details>


### [91] [The Lee-Yang property of isotropic vector ferromagnets and lattice fields](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18675)
*Yuri Kozitsky*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper proves the generalized Lee-Yang property for isotropic spin and quantum field models on the one-dimensional integer lattice ℤ for all even spatial dimensions D.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The Lee-Yang property—characterized by purely imaginary zeros of the partition function in the complex magnetic field plane—is a powerful analytic tool in statistical mechanics and quantum field theory; however, its rigorous establishment has been limited to two-dimensional isotropic models, leaving a gap for lower (especially 1D) and higher even-D cases.

Method: Rigorous mathematical analysis employing complex analysis and representation-theoretic properties of isotropic O(D)-invariant spin models; specifically, the authors extend known techniques for D=2 to general even D by leveraging symmetry, moment generating function structure, and zero-free region arguments in the complex external field plane.

Result: The generalized Lee-Yang property is rigorously established for classical isotropic spin models and quantum anharmonic crystal / lattice field models defined on ℤ with O(D)-symmetry, for all even D ≥ 2.

Conclusion: The result significantly broadens the domain of validity of the Lee-Yang property beyond two dimensions, enabling new applications of Lee-Yang-type methods to 1D quantum and statistical systems with continuous rotational symmetry in even internal dimensions.

Abstract: The Lee-Yang property of a given spin model means that its partition function has purely imaginary zeros as a function of an external magnetic field. A similar property is also used in the theory of quantum anharmonic crystals and quantum lattice fields. A number of powerful analytic methods of the mathematical theory of such models employ this property. Its suitable generalization is used in the theory of models of isotropic $D$-dimensional spins (rotors) or $D$-component quantum lattice fields. So far, the (generalized) Lee-Yang property has been established only for two-dimensional isotropic models. In this work, we prove that isotropic spin and field models living on $\mathds{Z}$ have this property for all even $D$.

</details>


### [92] [Duality of generalized Maxwell theories as an equivalence in derived geometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19161)
*Chris Elliott,Owen Gwilliam,Ingmar Saberi,Brian R. Williams*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper introduces a non-perturbative, derived differential geometric framework for moduli spaces of p-form generalized Maxwell theories, unifying BV formalism and differential cohomology to establish Dirac charge quantization and abelian duality, and computes compactifications via sheaf-theoretic pushforwards.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To provide a rigorous, non-perturbative description of moduli spaces for generalized Maxwell theories—beyond standard gauge theory—by reconciling quantum field theoretic structures (BV formalism) with topological-geometric ones (differential cohomology), enabling precise treatment of charge quantization and duality.

Method: Employs derived differential geometry to model moduli spaces as derived stacks; integrates the Batalin–Vilkovisky (BV) formalism for gauge-invariant quantization with differential cohomology (via sheaves of cochain complexes); uses derived pushforwards along Riemannian manifolds to handle compactification.

Result: Constructs charge-quantized moduli spaces satisfying Dirac quantization; proves abelian duality between distinct p-form theories; computes compactified theories as pushforwards of differential cohomological sheaves, yielding effective lower-dimensional theories with controlled torsion and curvature data.

Conclusion: Derived differential geometry provides a unified, non-perturbative foundation for generalized Maxwell theories, naturally encoding quantization, duality, and dimensional reduction—thereby bridging mathematical physics, homotopical algebra, and differential topology.

Abstract: We propose a non-perturbative description of the moduli spaces encoding p-form generalized Maxwell theories in any dimension, using derived differential geometry. Our approach synthesizes the Batalin--Vilkovisky formalism with differential cohomology. Within this framework we formulate Dirac charge quantization and show how such charge-quantized moduli spaces exhibit abelian duality between generalized Maxwell theories of different types. We also describe the compactification of generalized Maxwell theories along closed Riemannian manifolds by computing the pushforward of the underlying sheaves of cochain complexes that model differential cohomology.

</details>
